Given that  $\overline{\mathcal{I}}$ ,  $\overline{\mathcal{Y}}$  and  $i^*$  are fixed, we observe that  $y^* = \alpha + \beta \cdot y_t$  where  $\alpha, \beta \in \mathbb{F}$  are constants. Additionally, since  $i^*$ ,  $i_t$  and the indices in  $\overline{\mathcal{I}}$  are all distinct, we have that  $\beta \neq 0$  and thus the map  $f(X) = \alpha + \beta \cdot X$  is a bijection from  $\mathbb{F}$  to  $\mathbb{F}$ . Hence, since  $y_t$  is uniform, we have that  $y^*$  is uniform and independent of  $n, t, \overline{\mathcal{I}}, i_t, i^*, \overline{\mathcal{Y}}$ . The theorem follows.

Note that the above lemma does not assume any distribution on the evaluations, except that one of them is random.

## 4 Evolving Threshold Access Structures without Weights

Below, we recall the formal definition of an evolving threshold access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\text{ethr}}$ . We adopt the more general definition provided by [13, Remark 4] where threshold can be arbitrary (i.e., they can increase, decrease, or remain stable). In order to be monotone and rigid, the reconstructing threshold  $t_n$  of an authorized set  $\mathcal{I}$  is the one associated to the party with the largest index in  $\mathcal{I}$ , as defined in [13, Remark 4].

<span id="page-22-1"></span>**Definition 16 (Evolving Threshold Access Structure [13,14]).** An evolving threshold access structure  $\hat{A}^{\text{ethr}}$  is defined over a sequence of thresholds  $t_1, \ldots, t_n$  satisfying the following condition:

- (qualified set) a set  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, \dots, i_k, n\}$  is qualified (i.e.,  $\mathcal{I} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{ethr}}$ ) if  $t_n \leq |\mathcal{I}|$  and  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$ .

We note that the above access structure is monotone and rigid by definition. Monotonicity holds since any superset  $\mathcal{I}'$  of a qualified set  $\mathcal{I}$  is authorized by definition, as  $\mathcal{I}'$  necessarily contains  $\mathcal{I}$ , which satisfies both  $t_n \leq |\mathcal{I}|$  and  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$ . Rigidity holds by the constraint  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$  whose value determines the reconstructing threshold  $t_n$ . This implies that any unauthorized set  $\mathcal{I}$  such that  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$  but  $|\mathcal{I}| < t_n$  remains unauthorized, since the threshold  $t_n$  always applies to  $\mathcal{I}$  when n is the party with the highest index.

### 4.1 Construction from iO for Turing Machines and PPRF

<span id="page-22-0"></span>We are now ready to present our construction of ESS for the dynamic threshold evolving access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\text{ethr}}$  with share size  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log n)$ , where n is the number of parties. In Figure 1 we provide the formalization of our Turing machine whereas in Construction 4.1 we present our ESS scheme.

{23}------------------------------------------------

```
M_p^{\sf share}[\overline{K_f,i,\mathsf{pos},t^*,v](k,t)}:
 1: if k < i or t \le 0 then
 2:
         \operatorname{return} \boldsymbol{\perp}
 3: if k = pos and t = t^* then
 4:
         return v
 5: Initialize tape eval as an array of evaluations of size t.
 6: j = 0
 7: while j < t do
         eval[j] = Eval(K_f, k||t||(2^{\lambda} - j))
 8:
 9:
         j = j + 1
10: j = 0, S = 0
11: while j < t do
12:
         m = 0, L = 1
         while m < t do
13:
             if m \neq j then
14:
                  L = L \cdot \frac{i - (2^{\lambda} - m)}{(2^{\lambda} - j) - (2^{\lambda} - m)} \mod p
15:
              m = m + 1
16:
         S = S + L \cdot \mathsf{eval}[j] \bmod p
17:
         j = j + 1
18:
19: return S
```

<span id="page-23-0"></span>**Fig. 1.** The formal definition of the Turing Machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, v](k, t)$  required in Construction 4.1. The input space of the machine is  $\{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}$ . Given the description, it is syntactically clear that  $M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, v](k, t)$ , for any input  $(k, t) \in \{0, 1\}^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}$ , the machine always halt. We denote by  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} = 2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$  and  $t_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  the maximum input size and maximum running time (over the choice of all inputs  $(k, t) \in \{0, 1\}^{\ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}}$ ). The highlighted parts of the Turing machine are those required to prove the security of the scheme (due to the use of iO), and are therefore not needed for correctness.

{24}------------------------------------------------

#### **Construction 4.1**

Consider the following ingredients:

- $\mathbb{F}_p$  be a field where p is a  $(\lambda + 1)$ -bit prime;
- PPRF = (KeyGen, Punc, Eval) be a PPRF such that Eval :  $\{0,1\}^{\lambda} \times \{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda} \to \mathbb{F}_p;^a$
- Obf be an iO obfuscator for the class of Turing machines  $\mathcal{M}^{\mathsf{share}} = \{M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, v](k, t)\}$  as defined in Figure 1. The values between square brackets are hardcoded values that we will modify during our security proof. The hardcoded values come from the space  $\mathsf{KeyGen}(1^\lambda) \times \{0, 1\}^{3 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)} \times \mathbb{F}_p$ .

We build a ESS scheme SS = (Share, Recon) over message space  $\mathbb{F}_p$  for the evolving threshold access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{ethr}$  (Definition 16) as follows:

**Sharing:** When the *n*-th party arrives, the dealer shares  $\mu \in \mathbb{F}_p$  as follows:

- If n = 1 (first party), sample a PPRF key  $K_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- Let  $M_n = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, n, 0, 0, 0](\cdot, \cdot)$  be a Turing machine as defined in Figure 1 and let  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  and  $t_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  be the maximum input size and running time defined in Figure 1.
- Compute  $\widetilde{M}_n \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_n)$ .
- Compute  $K_n = f_n(0)$ , where  $f_n(\bar{X}) \in \mathbb{F}_p$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_n-1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\{\text{Eval}(K_f, n||t_n||(2^{\lambda}-j))\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$  and the points  $\{2^{\lambda}-j\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$ .
- Compute  $\operatorname{ct}_n = K_n \cdot \mu$  where  $\mu$  is the message.
- Finally, set the share of the *n*-th party to  $\sigma_n = (\mathsf{ct}_n, \widetilde{M}_n)$ .

**Reconstruction:** The reconstruction algorithm  $\mathsf{Recon}((\sigma_i)_{i \in \mathcal{I}}, \mathcal{I}, \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{ethr}})$ , given the shares  $(\sigma_i)_{i \in \mathcal{I}} = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ , and a (minimal) qualified subset  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, i_2, \ldots, n\} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{ethr}}$  (i.e.,  $|\mathcal{I}| \geq t_n$  and  $\mathsf{max}(\mathcal{I}) = n$ ), it proceeds as follows:

- For  $i \in \mathcal{I}$ , execute the obfuscated Turing machine  $\mathsf{sh}_i = \widetilde{M}_i(n, t_n)$ .
- Compute  $K'_n = \mathsf{Lagrange}(0, (\mathsf{sh}_i)_{i \in \mathcal{I}}, \mathcal{I})$ .
- Finally, output  $\mu' = \operatorname{ct}_n \cdot (K'_n)^{-1}$ .

Correctness, succinctness, and security of Construction 4.1. Correctness follows by the correctness of iO. The formal proof is deferred to Appendix A.1.

**Theorem 4.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is correct (Definition 8) then the ESS scheme of Construction 4.1 is perfectly correct.

<span id="page-24-1"></span><span id="page-24-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>a</sup> Note that  $suplog(\lambda)$  bits are sufficient to encode in binary any number of parties  $n \in poly(\lambda)$  and any threshold  $t_n \leq n$ .

{25}------------------------------------------------

As for succinctness, we demonstrate that obfuscating Mshare p [K<sup>f</sup> , i, pos, t<sup>∗</sup> , v]( k, t) produces an obfuscation of size poly(λ, log n) (yielding a share of the same size). Below, we provide the formal result.

<span id="page-25-2"></span>Theorem 5. If the iO obfuscator Obf is succinct and efficient (Definition [10\)](#page-18-1) and PPRF is succinct and efficient (Definition [3\)](#page-16-0) then the ESS scheme of Construction [4.1](#page-22-0) produces shares of size poly(λ, log n) for every party n ≥ 1.

The formal proof is deferred to Appendix [A.2.](#page-35-1)

<span id="page-25-3"></span>Finally, the theorem below establishes the security of the scheme whose formal proof appears in Appendix [A.3](#page-36-0)

Theorem 6. If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition [9\)](#page-18-2), and PPRF is secure (Definition [2\)](#page-15-0), then the scheme ESS of Construction [4.1,](#page-22-0) for the evolving threshold access structures Aˆethr, is computationally private in the adaptive setting (Definition [15\)](#page-20-1).

## 5 Evolving Threshold Access Structures with Fixed Weights

We now focus on weighted threshold access structures under the restriction that weights are fixed. In a nutshell, when a party arrives, it is associated with a threshold t<sup>n</sup> and a weight wn, which remain unchanged throughout the entire evolution of the access structure (i.e., the n-th party always has weight wn). As in Aˆethr (Definition [16\)](#page-22-1), the reconstructing threshold t<sup>n</sup> is determined by the party with the highest index in the qualified set I.

<span id="page-25-1"></span>Definition 17 (Evolving Threshold Access Structure with Fixed Weights).

An evolving threshold access structure with fixed weights Aˆfw−ethr is defined over a sequence of threshold and weight pairs (t1, w1), . . . ,(tn, wn) satisfying the following condition:

- (qualified set) a set 
$$\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, \dots, i_k, n\}$$
 is qualified (i.e.,  $\mathcal{I} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}}$ ) if  $t_n \leq \sum_{i \in \mathcal{I}} w_i$  and  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$ .

We observe that also for this access structure (as for the one of Definition [16\)](#page-22-1), both monotonicity and rigidity are satisfied by definition.

### 5.1 Construction from iO for Turing Machines and PPRF

We are now ready to present our construction of ESS for the dynamic threshold evolving access structure with fixed weights Aˆfw−ethr with share size poly(λ, log W), where W is the sum of the parties' weights.

<span id="page-25-0"></span>We restrict ourselves to access structures Aˆfw−ethr in which each weight has size at most |w| = O(log λ). In Figure [2](#page-26-0) we provide the formalization of our Turing machine whereas in Construction [5.1](#page-25-0) we present our ESS scheme.

{26}------------------------------------------------

```
M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f,K_p,K_p',K_{p,i},W,W^*,w_i,i,\mathsf{pos},t^*,x_1,v_1,x_2,v_2,l^*,q_1^*,q_2^*](k,t,q):
1: if k < i or t \le 0 or q \le 0 or q > w_i then
 2:
         \operatorname{return} \perp
 3: Initialize tapes eval and points as arrays of evaluations and points of size t.
 4: j = 0
 5: if k = pos \text{ and } t = t^* \text{ and } q = q_1^* \text{ then}
         return (x_1, v_1)
 6:
 7: if k = pos \text{ and } t = t^* \text{ and } q \leq q_2^* \text{ then}
         return (Eval(K'_p, k||t||(W^* + q)), Eval(K_f, k||t||(W^* + q)))
 8:
9: if k = pos \text{ and } t = t^* \text{ then}
         while j < l^* do
10:
              eval[j] = Eval(K_f, k||t||j)
11:
             points[j] = Eval(K'_p, k||t||j)
12:
             j = j + 1
13:
         if v_2 \neq \bot then
14:
              eval[j] = v_2
15:
16:
              points[j] = x_2
17:
              j = j + 1
18: while j < t do
         eval[j] = Eval(K_f, k||t||(2^{\lambda} - j))
19:
         \mathsf{points}[j] = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k||t||(2^{\lambda} - j))
20:
21:
         j = j + 1
22: j = 0, S = 0
23: while j < t do
         m = 0, L = 1
24:
         while m < t do
25:
26:
              if m \neq j then
                  L = L \cdot \frac{\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,i}, k || t || (W+q)) - \mathsf{points}[m]}{\mathsf{points}[j] - \mathsf{points}[m]} \bmod p
27:
28:
              m = m + 1
         S = S + L \cdot \mathsf{eval}[j] \bmod p
29:
30:
         j = j + 1
31: return (Eval(K_{p,i}, k||t||(W+q)), S)
```

<span id="page-26-0"></span>Machine Fig. 2. The formal definition of Turing the  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, q) \quad \mathsf{required}$ in Construction 5.1. The input space of the machine is  $\{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + |w|}$  where |w|is the maximum supported weight size. Given the description, it is syntactically clear  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, q),$ that for any input  $(k,t,q) \in \{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + |w|}$ , the machine always halt. We denote by  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} = 2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + |w| \text{ and } t_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} \text{ the maximum input size and maximum}$ running time (over the choice of all inputs  $(k, t, q) \in \{0, 1\}^{\ell_{M}^{\text{max}} + \text{share}}$ ). The highlighted parts of the Turing machine are those required to prove the security of the scheme (due to the use of iO), and are therefore not needed for correctness.

{27}------------------------------------------------

#### Construction 5.1

Consider the following ingredients:

- $-\mathbb{F}_p$  be a field where p is a  $(\lambda + 1)$ -bit prime;
- PPRF = (KeyGen, Punc, Eval) be a PPRF such that Eval :  $\{0,1\}^{\lambda}$  ×  $\{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda} \to \mathbb{F}_n; a$
- Obf be an iO obfuscator for the class of Turing machines  $\mathcal{M}^{\mathsf{fw-share}} =$  $\{M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, The values between square brackets are the hardcoded values that we will modify during our security proof. The hardcoded values come from the following space  $KeyGen(1^{\lambda})^4 \times$  $\{0,1\}^{2\cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + |w| + 3\cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda)} \times \mathbb{F}_p^4 \times \{0,1\}^{3\cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda)}.$

We build a ESS scheme SS = (Share, Recon) over message space  $\mathbb{F}_p$  for the evolving threshold access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\text{fw-ethr}}$  (Definition 17) for weights of size  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$  as follows:

**Sharing:** When the *n*-th party arrives, the dealer proceeds as follows:

- If n = 1 (first party), sample four PPRF keys:  $K_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), K_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow}$  $\mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), \, K'_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), \, \mathrm{and} \, K_{p,n} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}).^b$
- Let  $M_n = M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K'_p, K_p, W_{n-1}, 0, w_n, n, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, \bot, 0, 0, 0]$  $(\cdot,\cdot,\cdot)$  be a Turing machine as defined in Figure 2 and let  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw-share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  and  $t_{M^{\mathsf{fw-share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  are the maximum input size and running time defined in Figure 2.
- Compute  $\widetilde{M}_n \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{hare}}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_n).$
- Compute  $K_n = f_n(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||0))$ , where  $f_n(X) \in \mathbb{F}_p$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_n - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\{\operatorname{\mathsf{Eval}}(K_f,n||t_n||(2^{\lambda}-j))\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$  and the points  $\{\operatorname{\mathsf{Eval}}(K_p,n||t_n||(2^{\lambda}-j))\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$  $j))\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}.$
- Compute  $\mathsf{ct}_n = K_n \cdot \mu$  where  $\mu$  is the message.
- Finally, set the share of the *n*-th party to  $\sigma_n = (\mathsf{ct}_n, M_n, x_{n,0})$  where  $x_{n,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||0).$

**Reconstruction:** The reconstruction algorithm  $\mathsf{Recon}((\sigma_i)_{i\in\mathcal{I}},\mathcal{I},\hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}}),$ given the shares  $(\sigma_i)_{i\in\mathcal{I}} = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , and a (minimal) qualified subset  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, i_2, \dots, n\} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}} \text{ (i.e., } W_{\mathcal{I}} = \sum_{i \in \mathcal{I}} w_i \ge t_n \text{ and } \mathsf{max}(\mathcal{I}) = n), \text{ it}$ proceeds as follows:

- For every  $i \in \mathcal{I}$  and  $q_i \in [w_i]$ , execute the obfuscated Turing machine  $(x_{i,q_i},\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i}) = M_i(n,t_n,q_i).$
- Run  $K'_n$  = Lagrange $(x_{n,0}, (\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]}, (x_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]})$ . Finally, output  $\mu' = \mathsf{ct}_n \cdot (K'_n)^{-1}$ .

{28}------------------------------------------------

Correctness, succinctness, and security of Construction 5.1. Differently from Construction 4.1, Construction 5.1 does not achieve perfect correctness. This is because correctness requires that all points, generated as  $\{x_{i,q_i} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,i}, n || t_n || (W+q_i))\} \cup \{\operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,i}, n || t_n || (2^{\lambda}-j))\}$  by the set of Turing Machins  $\{\widetilde{M}_i(n, t_n, q_i)\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}}$  are distinct. This property follows from the security of the underlying PPRF. Below, we provide the formal statement, while the proof is given in Appendix A.4.

<span id="page-28-3"></span>**Theorem 7.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is correct (Definition 8) and PPRF is secure (Definition 2) then the ESS scheme of Construction 5.1 is correct.

As for succinctness, we demonstrate that obfuscating  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*]$  produces an obfuscation of size  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log W_n)$  (yielding a share of the same size) where  $\sum_{i \in [n]} w_i = W_n$ . Below, we provide the formal result, whose proof appears in Appendix A.5.

<span id="page-28-4"></span>**Theorem 8.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is succinct and efficient (Definition 10) and PPRF is succinct and efficient (Definition 3) then the ESS scheme of Construction 5.1 produces shares of size  $poly(\lambda, \log W_n)$  where  $\sum_{i \in [n]} w_i = W_n$  for every party  $n \geq 1$ .

<span id="page-28-5"></span>Finally, the theorem below establishes the security of the scheme whose formal proof appears in Appendix A.6.

**Theorem 9.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition 9) and PPRF is secure (Definition 2), then the scheme ESS scheme of Construction 5.1, for the evolving threshold access structure with fixed weights  $\hat{A}^{\text{fw-ethr}}$  with weights of size at most  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ , is computationally private in the adaptive setting (Definition 15).

<span id="page-28-2"></span>Remark 1 (On supporting a priori unknown but logarithmic weight sizes  $|w| \in O(\log \lambda)$ ). Whereas we presented Construction 5.1 assuming a known upper bound |w| on all weight sizes, it is straightforward to see that the construction naturally supports weights whose size is a priori unknown but logarithmic in  $\lambda$ .

This can be achieved by slightly enlarging the hardcoded value space and the input space of the Turing Machine  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, q)$ . In particular, we can set  $q \in \{0, 1\}^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}$  (input of  $M_i$ ) and  $w_i \in \{0, 1\}^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}$  (hardcoded value of  $M_i$ ). In this way, the Turing Machine is able to handle weights of a priori unknown size  $|w| \in O(\log \lambda)$ , since any weight of logarithmic size can be encoded using  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$ .

The proof of correctness, succinctness, and security of the related ESS scheme remains unaffected by this modification.

<span id="page-28-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>a</sup> Note that  $suplog(\lambda)$  bits are sufficient to encode in binary any number of parties  $n \in poly(\lambda)$  and any threshold  $t_n \leq n$ .

<span id="page-28-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>b</sup> The PPRF key  $K_{p'}$  is sampled and hardcoded into  $M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K'_p, K_{p,n}, W_{n-1}, 0, w_n, n, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0, 0]$  solely to simplify the security proof. Indeed,  $K'_p$  is used only in the proof and not required for the correctness of the construction.

{29}------------------------------------------------

### 6 Evolving Threshold Access Structures with Dynamic Weights

Our last construction tackles the most general notion of dynamic thresholds, denoted by Aˆdw−ethr. Here, the weights associated with parties may change over time, and the association in force is determined by the party with the largest index in the qualified set I. In a nutshell, when the n-th party arrives, it is associated with a threshold t<sup>n</sup> and a weight function weight<sup>n</sup> : [n] → N, which specifies the weight of the new n-th party and redefines the weights of all previous parties with index < n. Both the threshold t<sup>n</sup> and the weight function weight<sup>n</sup> are considered whenever n is the highest-index party participating in the reconstruction. The formal definition follows.

<span id="page-29-1"></span>Definition 18 (Evolving Threshold Access Structure supporting Dynamic Weights [\[12\]](#page-34-4)). An evolving threshold access structure with dynamic weights Aˆdw−ethr is defined over a sequence of weights functions and threshold pairs (weight<sup>1</sup> , t1), . . . ,(weightn, tn) satisfying the following condition:

```
– (qualified set) a set I = {i1, . . . , ik, n} is authorized (i.e., I ∈ Aˆdw−ethr
                                                                          n
                                                                                 ) if
  tn ≤
        P
          j∈I weightn(j) and max(I) = n.
```

We observe that, when party n arrives, the threshold and the weights of all parties i < n may arbitrarily change. However, for any qualified set I ∈ An, the reconstruction uses the threshold and weight functions corresponding to the maximal index in the set I. This automatically preserves both monotonicity and rigidity.

### 6.1 Construction from iO for Turing Machines, PPRF, and SSB

In Figure [3](#page-30-0) we provides the formalization of our Turing machine whereas in Construction [6.1](#page-29-0) we present our last ESS scheme.

<span id="page-29-0"></span>As in Construction [5.1,](#page-25-0) this construction supports the evolving access structure Aˆdw−ethr (Definition [18\)](#page-29-1) with weights of size |w| = O(log λ). We note that the scheme below assumes an a priori known bound |w| = O(log λ). Nevertheless, the scheme is able to support also weights of a priori unknown but logarithmic size by applying the same technique described in Remark [1](#page-28-2) of Construction [5.1.](#page-25-0) We recall that this construction achieves static privacy only, due to the use of SSB. We refer the reader to the technical overview for more details.

{30}------------------------------------------------

```
M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W^*, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, h, \pi, w, q) :
 1: if k < i or t \le 0 then
 2:
         return \perp
 3: if 0 = SSB. Verify(hk, h, i, w, \pi) or q \le 0 or q > w then
         return \perp
 4:
 5: if k = pos and t = t^* and q = q_1^* then
         return (x_1, v_1)
 6:
 7: if k = pos \text{ and } t = t^* \text{ and } q \leq q_2^* \text{ then }
 8:
         return (Eval(K'_p, k||t||h||(W^* + q)), Eval(K_f, k||t||h||(W^* + q)))
 9: Initialize tapes eval and points as arrays of evaluations and points of size t
10: j = 0
11: if k = pos \text{ and } t = t^* \text{ then }
12:
          while j < l^* do
13:
              eval[j] = Eval(K_f, k||t||h||j)
              points[j] = Eval(K'_n, k||t||h||j)
14:
15:
              j = j + 1
16:
         if v_2 \neq \bot then
17:
              eval[j] = v_2
18:
              points[j] = x_2
19:
              j = j + 1
20: while j < t do
         \operatorname{eval}[j] = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, k||t||h||(2^{\lambda} - j))
21:
         points[j] = Eval(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{\lambda} - j))
22:
23:
         j = j + 1
24: j = 0, S = 0
25: while j < t do
26:
         m = 0, L = 1
27:
          while m < t do
28:
              if m \neq j then
                   L = L \cdot \frac{\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k || t || h || (2^{i\lambda} + q)) - \mathsf{points}[m]}{\mathsf{points}[j] - \mathsf{points}[m]} \bmod p
29:
30:
              m = m + 1
31:
          S = S + L \cdot \mathsf{eval}[j] \bmod p
32:
         j = j + 1
33: return (Eval(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{i\lambda} + q)), S)
```

<span id="page-30-0"></span>Fig. 3. definition The formal of the Turing Machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}[K_f,K_p,K_p',\mathsf{hk},W^*,i,\mathsf{pos},t^*,x_1,v_1,x_2,v_2,l^*,q_1^*,q_2^*](k,t,h,\pi,w,q)$ required in Construction 6.1. The input space of the machine is  $\{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \ell_{\mathsf{hash}} + \ell_{\mathsf{open}} + 2 \cdot |w|}$ where  $\ell_{\text{open}}$  and  $\ell_{\text{hash}}$  are the sizes of opening and hashes produced by SSB, and |w|is the maximum supported weight size. Given the description, it is syntactically clear that  $M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W^*, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$ , for any input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q) \in \{0, 1\}^{2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + \ell_{\mathsf{hash}} + \ell_{\mathsf{open}} + 2 \cdot |w|}$ , the machine always halt. We denote by  $\ell_{M^{\sf dw-share}}^{\sf max} = 2 \cdot {\sf suplog}(\lambda) + \ell_{\sf hash} + \ell_{\sf open} + 2 \cdot |w|$  and  $t_{M^{\sf dw-share}}^{\sf max}$  be its maximum input size and maximum running time (over the choice of all inputs  $(k,t,h,\pi,w,q) \in \{0,1\}^{\ell_{M^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}}$ ). The highlighted parts of the Turing machine are those required to prove the security of the scheme (due to the use of iO), and are therefore not needed for correctness.

{31}------------------------------------------------

#### **Construction 6.1**

Consider the following ingredients:

- $\mathbb{F}_p$  be a field where p is a  $(\lambda^c)$ -bit prime for constant c > 1;
- SSB = (Setup, Hash, Open, Verify) be an SSB scheme. Let  $\ell_{\mathsf{block}}$ ,  $\ell_{\mathsf{open}}$ ,  $\ell_{\mathsf{hash}}$  be the length of a block length, proofs  $\pi$ , and hashes of SSB. Since the SSB block will be the encoding of a weight of size  $O(\log \lambda)$ , we set  $\ell_{\mathsf{block}} = |w|$  where  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$  is the maximum supported weight bit size;
- PPRF = (KeyGen, Punc, Eval) be a PPRF such that Eval :  $\{0,1\}^{\lambda} \times \{0,1\}^{2 \cdot \text{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda + \ell_{\text{hash}}} \to \mathbb{F}_p; a$
- Obf be an iO obfuscator for the class of Turing machines  $\mathcal{M}^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}} = \{M_p^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}[K_f,K_p,K_p',\mathsf{hk},W^*,i,\mathsf{pos},t^*,x_1,v_1,x_2,v_2,l^*,q_1^*,q_2^*](k,t,h,\pi,w,q)\}$  as defined in Figure 3. The values between square brackets are hardcoded values that we will modify during our security proof. The hardcoded values come from the following space  $\mathsf{KeyGen}(1^\lambda)^3 \times \mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda) \times \{0,1\}^{4\cdot\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)} \times \mathbb{F}_p^4 \times \{0,1\}^{3\cdot\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}$ .

We build a ESS scheme SS = (Share, Recon) over message space  $\mathbb{F}_p$  for the evolving threshold access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{dw-ethr}$  (Definition 18) with weights of size at most  $O(\log \lambda) = |w|$  as follows:

**Sharing:** When the n-th party arrives, the dealer proceeds as follows:

- If n=1 (first party), sample  $K_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), K_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), K_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}),$  and  $\mathsf{hk} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{\mathsf{block}}}, 2^{\lambda}, 1).$
- Let  $M_n = M_p^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, 0, n, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, \bot, 0, 0, 0](\cdot, \cdot, \cdot, \cdot, \cdot, \cdot)$  be a Turing machine as defined in Figure 3 and let  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  and  $t_{M^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$  be the maximum input size and running time defined in Figure 3.
- Compute  $\widetilde{M}_n \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{M\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_n)$ .
- Compute  $h_n = \mathsf{Hash}(\mathsf{hk}, (\mathsf{weight}_n(i))_{i \in [n]})$ .
- Compute  $K_n = f_n(\operatorname{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||h_n||0))$ , where  $f_n(X) \in \mathbb{F}_p$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_n 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\{\operatorname{Eval}(K_f, n||t_n||h_n||(2^{\lambda} j))\}_{j \in [0, t_n)}$  and the points  $\{\operatorname{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||h_n||(2^{\lambda} j))\}_{j \in [0, t_n)}$ .
- Compute  $\operatorname{ct}_n = K_n \cdot \mu$  where  $\mu$  is the message.
- Finally, set the share of the *n*-th party to  $\sigma_n = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_n, \widetilde{M}_n, x_{n,0})$  where  $x_{n,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||h_n||0).$

**Reconstruction:** The reconstruction algorithm  $\mathsf{Recon}((\sigma_i)_{i \in \mathcal{I}}, \mathcal{I}, \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}})$ , given the shares  $(\sigma_i)_{i \in \mathcal{I}} = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , and a (minimal) qualified subset  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, i_2, \dots, n\} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}}$  (i.e.,  $W_{\mathcal{I}} = \sum_{i \in \mathcal{I}} \mathsf{weight}_n(i) \geq t_n$  and  $\mathsf{max}(\mathcal{I}) = n$ ), it proceeds as follows:

{32}------------------------------------------------

- Let (weight<sub>n</sub>,  $t_n$ ) be the weights function and threshold pair which is part of the definition of the access structure  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}}$  taken as input.
- Compute  $h_n = \mathsf{Hash}(\mathsf{hk}, (\mathsf{weight}_n(i))_{i \in [n]})$ .
- For every  $i \in \mathcal{I}$  and  $q_i \in [w_i]$ , execute the obfuscated Turing machine  $(x_{i,q_i}\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i}) = \widetilde{M}_i(n,t_n,h_n,\pi_i,\mathsf{weight}_n(i),q_i)$  where  $\pi_i = \mathsf{Open}(\mathsf{hk},$  $(\mathsf{weight}_n(i))_{i \in [n]}, i).$
- Compute  $K'_n = \mathsf{Lagrange}(x_{n,0}, (\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]}, (x_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]}).$  Finally, output  $\mu' = \mathsf{ct}_n \cdot (K'_n)^{-1}.$
- <span id="page-32-0"></span><sup>a</sup> Note that  $suplog(\lambda)$  bits are sufficient to encode in binary any number of parties  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and any threshold  $t_n \leq n$ .
- <span id="page-32-1"></span><sup>b</sup> The latter PPRF key  $K_{p'}$  is sampled and hardcoded into  $M_p^{\sf dw-share}[K_f, K_p, K_p', {\sf hk}, 0, n, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0, 0]$  solely to simplify the security proof. Indeed,  $K'_p$  is used only in the proof and not required for the correctness of the construction.

As for Construction 5.1, this construction does not achieve perfect correctness. Below, we report the formal statement whose proof appears in Appendix A.7.

<span id="page-32-2"></span>**Theorem 10.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is correct (Definition 8) and PPRF is secure (Definition 2) then the ESS scheme of Construction 6.1 is correct.

As usual, succinctness follows by demonstrating that  $M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p']$ hk, 0, n, 0, 0, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0, 0 produces an obfuscation of size poly( $\lambda, \log W_n$ ) (yielding a share of the same size) where  $\sum_{i \in [n]} \mathsf{weight}_n(i) = W_n$ . Below, we provide the formal result whose proof appears in Appendix A.8.

<span id="page-32-3"></span>**Theorem 11.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is succinct and efficient (Definition 10), PPRF is succinct and efficient (Definition 3), and SSB is succinct and efficient (Definition 7) then the ESS scheme of Construction 6.1 produces shares of size  $\operatorname{poly}(\lambda, \log W_n)$  where  $\sum_{i \in [n]} \operatorname{weight}_n(i) = W_n$  for every party  $n \geq 1$ .

<span id="page-32-4"></span>Finally, the theorem below establishes the security of the scheme whose formal proof appears in Appendix A.9. We recall that this construction only achieves static security.

**Theorem 12.** If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition 9) PPRF is secure (Definition 2), and SSB is index hiding (Definition 5) and somewhere perfectly binding (Definition 6), then the scheme ESS scheme of Construction 6.1, for the evolving threshold access structure with dynamic weights  $\hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{dw-ethr}}$  with weights of size at most  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ , is a computationally private in the static setting (Definition 15).

#### Supporting Proofs $\mathbf{A}$

#### Proof of Theorem 4 $\mathbf{A.1}$

<span id="page-35-0"></span>*Proof.* Let  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  and  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, i_2, \dots, n\} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{ethr}}$ , i.e.,  $|\mathcal{I}| \geq t_n$  and  $\mathsf{max}(\mathcal{I}) = n$ . Let us show  $(K'_n)^{-1} \cdot K_n \cdot \mu = \mu$ . First, we have  $K_n = \mathsf{Lagrange}(0, (\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, n | |t_n|)))$  $(2^{\lambda}-j))_{j\in[0,t_n)}, (2^{\lambda}-j)_{j\in[0,t_n)}).$ 

Each party  $i \in \mathcal{I}$  holds  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ , where  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ , with  $K_i = \mathsf{ct}_i$  $f_i(0)$  and  $\widetilde{M}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^\lambda, 1^{\ell_{M\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_i)$  with  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, 0, 0, 0](\cdot, \cdot)$ . During reconstruction, for each party  $i \in \mathcal{I}$ , we run the obfuscated program  $\mathsf{sh}_i = M_i(n,t_n)$ . By correctness of  $\mathsf{Obf}$ , this outputs the values generated by  $M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, v](k, t)$  which runs the code in figure 1 and has harcoded values:  $K_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), i = i, \mathsf{pos} = t^* = v = 0.$  Clearly  $n \geq i,$  and  $t_n > i$ 0. Then, the circuit computes for every  $j \in [0, t_n)$  the evaluations eval[j]Eval $(K_f, n||t_n||(2^{\lambda}-j))$ . Finally the circuit computes Lagrange $(i, (\text{eval}[j])_{j \in [0,t_n)},$  $(2^{\lambda} - j)_{j \in [0,t_n)}$ ). Hence, for every  $i \in \mathcal{I}$ , the parties obtain  $\mathsf{sh}_i = f_n(i)$ , and since  $\mathcal{I} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{ethr}}$ , we are guaranteed that parties collectively have at least  $t_n$ shares  $(\mathsf{sh}_i)_{i\in\mathcal{I}}$ . Thus, parties can compute  $K_n' = \mathsf{Lagrange}(0, (\mathsf{sh}_i)_{i\in\mathcal{I}}, \mathcal{I})$ , which is exactly  $f_n(0)$ . Finally, since  $K'_n = f_n(0) = K_n$ , we have that  $(K_n)^{-1} \cdot K_n \cdot \mu =$  $\mu$ .

#### Proof of Theorem 5 $\mathbf{A.2}$

<span id="page-35-1"></span>*Proof.* We need to prove that the size of each share  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$  is  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log i)$ . First, we have that  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ : Hence,  $|\mathsf{ct}_i| \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ . To conclude the proof, it remains to show that  $|\widetilde{M}_i|$  is in  $poly(\lambda, \log i)$ .

Recall that  $\widetilde{M}_i$  is computed as  $\widetilde{M}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^\lambda, 1^{\ell_{M\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M\mathsf{share}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_i)$  with  $M_i = 1$  $M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, v]$ . By the succinctness and efficiency requirements on  $\mathsf{Obf}$ ,  $|\widetilde{M}_i|$  is in  $\mathsf{poly}(|M_p^\mathsf{share}|, \log t_{M^\mathsf{share}}^\mathsf{max}, \ell_{M^\mathsf{share}}^\mathsf{max}, \lambda)$ , where:

- 1.  $|M_p^{\text{share}}|$  is the description size of the Turing Machine;
- 2.  $t_{M^{\text{share}}}^{\text{max}}$  is the maximum runtime of the Turing Machine; 3.  $\ell_{M^{\text{share}}}^{\text{max}}$  is the maximum input size of the Turing Machine.

According to Figure 1, we have  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} = 2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$ . Below, we measure the remaining two parameters.

Regarding the maximum runtime  $t_{M^{\text{share}}}^{\text{max}}$ :

- Comparisons with i, 0, pos,  $t^*$  can be executed in time poly(suplog( $\lambda$ ));
- Eval $(K_f, \cdot)$  can be executed in  $(2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda) \cdot \operatorname{poly}(\lambda) = \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda));$
- Since  $t \leq n$  and  $|n| \leq \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda)$ , the first while-loop has runtime  $2^{\operatorname{suplog}(\lambda)}$  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda));$
- Modular arithmetic in  $\mathbb{F}_p$  can be executed in time  $\operatorname{poly}(\log p) = \operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  since p is a prime of  $\lambda + 1$  bits;
- Since  $t \leq n$ , the last while-loop (line 11) has runtime in  $(2^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)})^2 \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) =$  $2^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)} \cdot \mathsf{polv}(\lambda)$ .

{36}------------------------------------------------

Hence, the maximum runtime is bounded by

$$t_{M^{\mathrm{share}}}^{\mathrm{max}} = O\left(2^{\mathrm{suplog}(\lambda)}\right) \cdot \mathrm{poly}(\lambda, \mathrm{suplog}(\lambda)).$$

Regarding the description size  $|M_p^{\sf share}|$ , we start observing that, as described in Construction 4.1, the sizes of hardwired values (which are part of the description of the Turing Machine) are  $|K_f| = |\mathsf{KeyGen}(1^\lambda)| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda), \ |i| = |\mathsf{pos}| = |t^*| = \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda), \ \text{and} \ |v| = \log p = \log(\lambda + 1) \ \text{since} \ v \in \mathbb{F}_p.$ 

Then, the computation performed by the Turing Machine can be described using the following size:

- Comparisons with  $i, 0, pos, t^*$  can be described in size  $poly(suplog(\lambda))$ ;
- Eval $(K_f, \cdot)$  can be described in  $(2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda));$
- Since  $t \leq n$  and  $|n| \in \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$ , the first while-loop has description size  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda))$ ;
- Modular arithmetic in  $\mathbb{F}_p$  can be described in size  $\mathsf{poly}(\log p) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ ;
- Since  $t \leq n$  and  $|n| \in \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$ , the second while-loop (line 11) can be described in size  $2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

We conclude that the description size is bounded by

$$|M_p^{\rm share}| = {\sf poly}(\lambda, {\sf suplog}(\lambda)).$$

By combining the bounds of  $|M_p^{\sf share}|,\,t_{M^{\sf share}}^{\sf max},$  and  $\ell_{M^{\sf share}}^{\sf max},$  we conclude:

$$\begin{split} |\widetilde{M}_i| &= \mathsf{poly}(|M_p^{\mathsf{share}}|, \log t_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \ell_{M^{\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \lambda) \\ &= \mathsf{poly}(\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)), O(\log(2^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)})) \\ &\quad \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)), 2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda), \lambda) \\ &= \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)). \end{split}$$

Finally, since  $i \in [n]$  for an apriori unknown  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  (and thus  $\log i = O(\log \lambda)$ ),  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) = \log^c(\lambda)$  for some constant c > 1, and all  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$  values are chosen so as to allow the Turing machine to perform its computation correctly for every pair (k,t) whose values can depend on n (i.e., worst-case size is  $O(\log n)$ ), for an apriori unknown value  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ , we can rewrite the equation above as follows:

$$|\widetilde{M}_i| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log i) \text{ where } i \in [n].$$

This concludes the proof.

#### A.3 Proof of Theorem 6

<span id="page-36-0"></span>Restatement of Theorem 6. If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition 9), and PPRF is secure (Definition 2), then the scheme ESS of Construction 4.1, for the evolving threshold access structures  $\hat{A}^{\text{ethr}}$ , is computationally private in the adaptive setting (Definition 15).

{37}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* Let  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  be the two messages chosen by the adversary A in the game defining the adaptive computational privacy of SS,  $G_{SS,A}^{priv}(\lambda, b)$ . W.l.o.g. we assume that on each adversary's oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{share}(n_g, \mathcal{U}), |\mathcal{U}| \leq 1$ .

Consider the following hybrid experiments.

 $\mathbf{H}_{0}(\lambda, b)$ : This experiment is identical to  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{A}}^{\mathsf{priv}}(\lambda, b)$ .

 $\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  (with  $\mathbf{H}_{19}^{0}(\lambda, b) = \mathbf{H}_{0}(\lambda, b)$ ), except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_{g}, z^{*})$ , if party  $z^{*} \leq i^{*}$  we change the machine used to generate  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  so that, on input  $(k, t) = (i^{*}, t_{i^{*}})$ , it outputs the explicitly hardwired value  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^{*}}^{t_{i^{*}}}$  (defined as  $\mathsf{Lagrange}(z^{*}, \{\mathsf{Eval}(K_{f}, i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda} - j))\}_{j \in [0, t_{i^{*}})}, \{2^{\lambda} - j\}_{j \in [0, t_{i^{*}})})$ ), and otherwise behaves as before. Hence, we replace the machine  $M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}$  we use to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  by

$$M_0 = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}]$$
 instead of  $M_1 = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, 0, 0, 0]$ .

 $\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$ , except that the challenger samples  $K_{f,*} = \mathsf{Punc}(K_{f}, \{i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||2^{\lambda}\})$  and we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_{g}, z^{*})$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  by

$$M_0 = \begin{cases} M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}] & \text{if } z^* \leq i^* \\ M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

instead of

$$M_{1} = \begin{cases} M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^{*}}^{t_{i^{*}}}] & \text{if } z^{*} \leq i^{*} \\ M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

 $\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$ , except that the challenger replaces the value  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||2^{\lambda})$  used in defining the polynomial  $f_{i^{*}}$  by a uniformly random value  $r_{i^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ . The key  $K_{i^{*}} = f_{i^{*}}(0)$ , and all the values  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_{j}}^{t_{i^{*}}} = f_{i^{*}}(z_{j})$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{j}}$  by the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  for all  $z_{j} \leq i^{*}$  are defined consistently as Lagrange interpolations of the resulting polynomial. Specifically,

$$K_{i^*} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{-x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

and

$$\mathsf{sh}_{z_j}^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{z_j - x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

{38}------------------------------------------------

with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} r_{i^*} & \text{if } j = 0\\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) & \text{if } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and  $x_j = 2^{\lambda} - j$  for all  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ .

 $\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$ , except that the challenger samples  $K_{i^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\lambda}$  instead of  $K_{i^{*}} = f_{i^{*}}(0)$ . All the values  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_{j}}^{t_{i^{*}}} = f_{i^{*}}(z_{j})$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{j}}$  by the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  for all  $z_{j} \leq i^{*}$ , are defined consistently as Lagrange interpolations of the resulting polynomial. Specifically,

$$\mathsf{sh}_{z_j}^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{z_j - x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} K_{i^*} \text{ if } j = 0 \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_j = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j = 0\\ 2^{\lambda} - j \text{ for all } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

 $\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_g, z^{*})$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  by

$$M_0 = \begin{cases} M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}] & \text{if } z^* \leq i^* \\ M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

instead of

$$M_{1} = \begin{cases} M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^{*}, i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^{*}}^{t_{i^{*}}}] & \text{if } z^{*} \leq i^{*} \\ M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^{*}, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

We will now run a series of hybrids:  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b),\ldots,\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and  $j^* \in [1,t_{i^*})$ :

-  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [1,t_{i^{*}})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^{*},j^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)$  with  $\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^{*},-1}(\lambda,b) = \mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that the challenger samples  $K_{f,*} = \mathsf{Punc}(K_{f},\{i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda}-j^{*})\})$  and we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_{g},z^{*})$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  by

instead of

$$M_{1} = \begin{cases} M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^{*}}^{t_{i^{*}}}] & \text{if } z^{*} \leq i^{*} \\ M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

-  $\mathbf{H}_{7}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [1,t_{i^{*}})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  as follows. We restrict attention to the subsequence of oracle queries  $\mathcal{Q} = (q_{1},\ldots,q_{m})$  made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , where each query  $q_{j}$  has parameters  $(n_{j},z_{j})$  with  $z_{j} \leq i^{*}$ ; all other queries with  $z_{j} > i^{*}$  are left unchanged.

When we reach the query  $q_{j^*} \in \mathcal{Q}$  (i.e., the  $j^*$ -th query with  $z_t \leq i^*$ ) the challenger replaces the value  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j^*))$  used in defining the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  by a uniformly random value  $r_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ .

$$\begin{cases} 0 & \text{if } j = 0 \end{cases}$$

We restrict attention to the subsequence of oracle queries  $\mathcal{Q} = (q_1,\ldots,q_m)$  made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , where each query  $q_j$  has parameters  $(n_j,z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ ; all other queries with  $z_j > i^*$  are left unchanged.

It then defines  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique degree  $t_{i^*}-1$  polynomial obtained by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$\mathsf{sh}_{z_j}^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{z_j - x_m}{x_j - x_m}.$$

-  $\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [1,t_{i^{*}})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{8}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_{g},z^{*})$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^{*}}$  by

restrict attention to the subsequence of oracle queries  $Q = (q_1, \ldots, q_m)$  made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$ , where each query  $q_j$  has parameters  $(n_j, z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ ; all other queries with  $z_j > i^*$  are left unchanged.

 $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,1}(\lambda, b)$ , except that the challenger samples  $K_{f,*} = \mathsf{Punc}(K_f, \{i^* || t_{i^*} || 2^{\lambda}\})$  and we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_g, z^*)$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^*}$  by
