and  $x_j = (2^{\lambda} - j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ . Consequently all values  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j}^{t_{i^*}}$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  by the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  are defined consistently as Lagrange interpolations of the resulting polynomial.

 $\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $K_{i^*}$ . In particular, the challenger computes  $K_{i^*} = \mathsf{Lagrange}(0, \{\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j))\}_{j \in [0, t_{i^*})}, \{2^{\lambda} - j\}_{j \in [0, t_{i^*})})$ . Moreover all values  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j}^{t_{i^*}}$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  by the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  are defined consistently as Lagrange interpolations of the resulting polynomial.

 $\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change

{43}------------------------------------------------

the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_g,z^*)$ , the challenger replaces the machine used to compute the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_{z^*}$  by

$$M_0 = \begin{cases} M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}] & \text{if } z^* \leq i^* \\ M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

instead of

$$M_1 = \begin{cases} M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}] & \text{if } z^* \leq i^* \\ M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

 $\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  such that, on input  $(n_g, z^*)$ , if party  $z^* \leq i^*$  we change the machine used to generate  $\widetilde{M}_{z^*}$  so that, on input  $(k, t) = (i^*, t_{i^*})$  the machine behaves normally instead of outputting the explicitly hardwired value  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}$ . In particular we let:

$$M_0 = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, 0, 0, 0]$$
 instead of  $M_1 = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}]$ 

<span id="page-43-0"></span>**Lemma 2.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* Let  $\mathcal{Q} = (q_1, \ldots, q_m)$  be the subsequence of oracle queries made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$ , where each query  $q_j$  has parameters  $(n_j, z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ ; for every  $z \in [0, |\mathcal{Q}|]$ , let  $\boldsymbol{H}_1^{i^*, z}(\lambda, b)$  be the experiment where we change the first z answers to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  with an input  $(n_g, z^*)$  such that  $z^* < i^*$ .

Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},|\mathcal{Q}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} = \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $z\in[|\mathcal{Q}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z^{*}}$  with  $z^{*}$  being the party corrupted in the z-th query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ .

Let us argue that

$$M_0 = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}]$$

and

$$M_1=M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_f,z^*,0,0,0]$$

are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input (k,t) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z^*$  and t > 0 must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ .

We distinguish 2 cases:

 $-k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ : In this case, in  $M_0$  we output  $v = \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}$ , while in  $M_1$  we output S. Notice that  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  and S are computed exactly at the same way, i.e., as the Lagrange interpolation in  $z^*$  of a degree  $t_{i^*} - 1$  polynomial evaluated at the  $t_{i^*}$  distinct points  $(2^{\lambda} - j)$  for  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ .

{44}------------------------------------------------

 $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output S.

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,z}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-44-0"></span>**Lemma 3.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, let  $q_{\text{max}}$  be the maximum number of queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{\text{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  made by the adversary. For every  $z \in [0, q_{\text{max}}]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,z}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change the first z answers to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\text{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ .

Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},q_{\mathsf{max}}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $z\in[q_{\mathsf{max}}]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c}\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z^{*}}$  with  $z^{*}$  being the party corrupted in the z-th query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ .

Let us argue that

$$M_0 = \begin{cases} M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*}^{t_{i^*}}] & \text{if } z^* \in \mathcal{U}^* \\ M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f,*}, z^*, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

and

$$M_{1} = \begin{cases} M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \mathsf{sh}_{z^{*}}^{t_{i^{*}}}] & \text{if } z^{*} \in \mathcal{U}^{*} \\ M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{f}, z^{*}, 0, 0, 0] & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input (k,t) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z^*$  and t > 0 must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ .

We distinguish 2 major cases:

- $-z^* > i^*$ : Since we assumed  $k \ge z^*$ ,  $k > i^*$  holds, and  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*))$  will never be called as the machine will abort;
- $-z^* \le i^*$ : here we distinguish two cases:
  - $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ : In this case, neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*))$  is never called, as both circuits output v;
  - $k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output S, without ever calling  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*))$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,z}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-44-1"></span>**Lemma 4.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

{45}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||2^{\lambda}$ . We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the pseudorandomness at punctured points of PPRF (Definition 2) as follows.

- The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  from the  $G_{SS,D}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary D.
- The reduction sends to the PPRF security game the point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||^{2^{\lambda}}$  and receives  $K_* = \operatorname{Punc}(K, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | 2^{\lambda}\})$  and either a uniform value  $\bar{u} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  or the value  $\bar{u} = \text{Eval}(K, i^* || t_{i^*} || 2^{\lambda})$ , where K is the PPRF key generated by the PPRF challenger.
- At each oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\sf share}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , on input  $(n_q,i)$  the oracle computes the answer  $\sigma_i$  as follows:
  - If  $i > i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} - j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} - j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:
    - \*  $\operatorname{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ ,
    - \*  $M_i = M_p^{\text{share}}[K_*, i, 0, 0, 0]$

Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .

• If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(0)$  and  $\mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}} = f_{i^*}(i^*)$  as

$$K_{i^*} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

and

$$\mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{i^* - x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \bar{u} \text{ if } j = 0\\ \text{Eval}(K_*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and  $x_j = 2^{\lambda} - j$  for all  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ . Then it sets:

- $\begin{array}{l} * \; \mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu, \\ * \; M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}}] \end{array}$

Finally  $\sigma_{i^*} = (\mathsf{ct}_{i^*}, M_{i^*}).$ 

• If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations Eval $(K_*,i||t_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda}-j)$  for all  $j\in[0,t_i)$  and  $\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}}=$  $f_{i^*}(i)$  as

$$\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{i-x_m}{x_j-x_m},$$

Then, it sets:

{46}------------------------------------------------

$$* \operatorname{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$$

- Finally, the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-46-0"></span>**Lemma 5.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by Lemma 1. We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the security of Lemma 1 as follows.

- The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{SS,D}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary D.
- The reduction computes  $K_* = \operatorname{Punc}(K_f, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | 2^{\lambda}\});$
- The reduction sends to the security game of Lemma 1:
  - $n = i^*$ ;
  - $t = t_{i^*}$ ;
  - $\mathcal{I} = \{2^{\lambda} j\}$  for  $j \in [1, t_{i^*})$  with  $|\mathcal{I}| = t_{i^*} 1$ ;
  - $i_{t-1} = 2^{\lambda}$ ;
  - $i^* = 0$ ;
  - $\mathcal{Y} = \{ \mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i^* | |t_{i^*}| | (2^{\lambda} j)) \} \text{ for } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \text{ with } |\mathcal{Y}| = t_{i^*} 1;$

Then, the Lemma 1 challenger randomly samples  $y_{t-1}$  and computes  $r_b$  either as a random value or as  $f(i^*) = \sum_{j=0}^{t-1} y_j \ell_{x_j}(i^*)$ , where  $\ell_{x_j}(x) = \prod_{\substack{0 \leq m \leq t-1 \\ m \neq x_j}} \frac{x-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$  (for  $i \in \mathcal{I}$ ). Then, it forwards  $r_b$  to the reduction. Then,

the reduction computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique polynomial of degree  $t_{i^*} - 1$  obtained by interpolating the values  $(y_j)_{j \in [0, t_{i^*})}$ :

$$y_j = \begin{cases} r_b \text{ if } j = 0 \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

at the points

$$x_j = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j = 0\\ 2^{\lambda} - j \text{ if } j \in [1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

- At each oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , on input  $(n_g,i)$  the oracle computes the answer  $\sigma_i$  as follows:
  - If  $i > i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:
    - $* \operatorname{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu,$
    - $*\ M_i = M_p^{\rm share}[K_*,i,0,0,0]$

Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .

{47}------------------------------------------------

• If  $i \leq i^*$ : the reduction computes  $\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}}$  as:

$$\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{i-x_m}{x_j-x_m},$$

Then:

\* If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*,i||t_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda}-j)$  for all  $j\in[0,t_i)$  and sets:

$$ct_{i} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$$

$$M_{i} = M_{p}^{\mathsf{share}}[K_{*}, i, i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \mathsf{sh}_{i}^{t_{i^{*}}}]$$
Finally  $\sigma_{i} = (\mathsf{ct}_{i}, \widetilde{M}_{i}).$ 
If  $i = i^{*}$ : the reduction sets:

\* If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction sets:

$$\begin{array}{l} \cdot \; \mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = r_b \cdot \mu \\ \cdot \; M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}}] \\ \mathrm{Finally} \; \sigma_{i^*} = (\mathsf{ct}_{i^*}, \widetilde{M}_{i^*}). \end{array}$$

- Finally the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-47-2"></span>**Lemma 6.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c}\{\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 3, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

<span id="page-47-0"></span>**Lemma 7.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)], j^* \in [1, t_{i^*}]$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}, it$ holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 3.

<span id="page-47-1"></span>**Lemma 8.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [1, t_{i^*})$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c}\{\mathbf{H}_{7}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the pseudorandomness at punctured points of PPRF (Definition 2) as follows.

- The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  from the  $G_{SS,D}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary D.
- The reduction sends to the PPRF security game the point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ and receives  $K_* = \operatorname{Punc}(K, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | (2^{\lambda} - j^*)\})$  and either a uniform value  $\bar{u} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  or the value  $\bar{u} = \mathsf{Eval}(K, i^* || t_{i^*} || 2^{\lambda} - j^*)$ , where K is the PPRF key generated by the PPRF challenger.
- At each oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\sf share}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , on input  $(n_q,i)$  the oracle computes the answer  $\sigma_i$  as follows:

{48}------------------------------------------------

- If  $i > i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\text{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:
  - \*  $\operatorname{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ ,
  - \*  $M_i = M_p^{\text{share}}[K_*, i, 0, 0, 0]$

Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .

- Otherwise, the reduction samples  $K_{i^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $j^*-1$  values  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}})_{j \in [1,j^*)}$  randomly, then for all the queries in which  $i \leq i^*$ :
  - \* For the queries  $q \in [1, j^*)$ :
    - · If  $i < i^*$ : The reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i_q}^{t_{i^*}}]$
    - · If  $i=i^*$ : the reduction sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*}=K_{i^*}\cdot\mu$ ,  $M_{i^*}=M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*,i^*,i^*,i^*,t_{i^*},\mathsf{sh}_{i_a}^{t_{i^*}}]$
    - · Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .
  - \* Otherwise, for the queries  $q \in [j^*, q_{\text{max}}]$ : the reduction computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique polynomial of degree  $t_{i^*} 1$  obtained by interpolating the values  $(y_j)_{j \in [0, t_{i^*})}$ :

$$y_j = \begin{cases} K_{i^*} \text{ if } j = 0\\ \text{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}} \text{ if } 0 < j < j^*\\ \bar{u} \text{ if } j = j^*\\ \text{Eval}(K_*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

at the points

$$x_j = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j = 0\\ i_j \text{ if } 0 < j < j^*\\ 2^{\lambda} - j \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

where  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}})_{j\in[1,j^*)}$  and  $(i_j)_{j\in[1,j^*)}$  are the randomly sampled shares and the indices of the corrupted parties during the queries  $q\in[1,j^*)$  respectively. The reduction also computes

$$\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{i-x_m}{x_j-x_m},$$

Then:

· If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} - j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} - j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_i \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}}]$ 

{49}------------------------------------------------

- · If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu$ ,  $M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}}]$ .
- · Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .
- Finally, the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-49-0"></span>**Lemma 9.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [1, t_{i^*})$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by Lemma 1. We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the security of Lemma 1 as follows.

- The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{D}}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary  $\mathsf{D}$ .
- The reduction computes  $K_* = \operatorname{Punc}(K_f, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | (2^{\lambda} j^*)\});$
- At each oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , on input  $(n_g,i)$  the oracle computes the answer  $\sigma_i$  as follows:
  - If  $i > i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:
    - \*  $\operatorname{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ ,
    - \*  $M_i = M_p^{\text{share}}[K_*, i, 0, 0, 0]$

Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .

- Otherwise, the reduction samples  $K_{i^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $j^*-1$  values  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}})_{j \in [1,j^*)}$  randomly, then for all the queries in which  $i \leq i^*$ :
  - \* For the queries  $q \in [1, j^*)$ :
    - · If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_i \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i_q}^{t_{i^*}}]$
    - · If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction sets:  $\operatorname{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu$ ,  $M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, sh_{i_q}^{t_{i^*}}]$
    - · Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .
  - \* At the query  $q = j^*$ : in order to simulate  $\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}}$  the reduction sends to the security game of Lemma 1:
    - $\cdot n = i^*;$
    - $t = t_{i^*};$

.

$$\mathcal{I} = \{ x_j \mid x_j = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j = 0\\ i_j \text{ if } 0 < j < j^*\\ 2^{\lambda} - j \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

for  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$  with  $|\mathcal{I}| = t_{i^*} - 1$ , where  $(i_j)_{j \in [1, j^*)}$  are the parties corrupted during the queries  $q \in [1, j^*)$ ;

 $\cdot i_{t-1} = 2^{\lambda} - j^*;$ 

{50}------------------------------------------------

 $\cdot i^* = i;$ 

$$\mathcal{Y} = \{y_j \mid y_j = \begin{cases} K_{i^*} \text{ if } j = 0\\ \operatorname{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}} \text{ if } 0 < j < j^*\\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

where  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}})_{j \in [1,j^*)}$  are the randomly sampled shares during the queries  $q \in [1,j^*)$ , with  $|\mathcal{Y}| = t_{i^*} - 1$ ;

Then, the Lemma 1 challenger randomly samples  $y_{t-1}$  and computes  $r_b$  either as a random value or as  $f(i^*) = \sum_{j=0}^{t-1} y_j \ell_{x_j}(i^*)$ , where  $\ell_{x_j}(x) = \prod_{\substack{0 \leq m \leq t-1 \\ m \neq x_j}} \frac{x-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$  (for  $i \in \mathcal{I}$ ). Then, it forwards  $r_b$  to the reduction. Then:

- · If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, r_b]$
- · If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction sets  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu$ ,  $M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, r_b]$ .
- · Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .
- \* For the queries  $q \in [j^* + 1, q_{\sf max}]$ : the reduction computes

$$\mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{i-x_m}{x_j-x_m},$$

with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} K_{i^*} \text{ if } j = 0\\ \mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}} \text{ if } 0 < j < j^*\\ r_b \text{ if } j = j^*\\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_{j} = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j = 0\\ i_{j} \text{ if } 0 < j < j^{*}\\ i \text{ if } j = j^{*}\\ 2^{\lambda} - j \text{ if } j \in [j^{*} + 1, t_{i^{*}}) \end{cases}$$

where  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i_j}^{t_{i^*}})_{j < j^*}$  and  $(i_j)_{j < j^*}$  are the randomly sampled shares and the parties corrupted during the queries  $q \in [1, j^*)$ . Then

· If  $i < i^*$ : the reduction computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i - 1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_*, i||t_i||(2^{\lambda} - j))$  at the points  $(2^{\lambda} - j)$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets:  $\mathsf{ct}_i \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_i^{t_{i^*}}]$ 

{51}------------------------------------------------

- · If  $i = i^*$ : the reduction sets  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu$ ,  $M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{share}}[K_*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, \mathsf{sh}_{i^*}^{t_{i^*}}]$ .
- · Finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i)$ .
- Finally the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-51-0"></span>**Lemma 10.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [1, t_{i^*})$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 7, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 11.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$  and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,t_{i^*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by observing that the two hybrids differ only in the answer of  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  on input  $(n_g, i^*)$ ; in the former hybrid  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu_b$  is a one-time-pad encryption under a uniform key  $K_{i^*}$ , while in the latter  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*}$  is sampled uniformly at random, which is identically distributed to a one-time-pad encryption.

**Lemma 12.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 1]$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*, j^* - 1}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of  $\mathsf{Obf}$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 10, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 13.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 1]$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Lemma 1. The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 9. We omit it for brevity.

**Lemma 14.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 1]$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 8. We omit it for brevity.

**Lemma 15.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 1]$  and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 7, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 16.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

{52}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 6, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 17.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Lemma 1. The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 5. We omit it for brevity.

**Lemma 18.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||2^{\lambda}$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 4. We omit it for brevity.

**Lemma 19.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 3, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 20.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 2, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 21.**  $\{\mathbf{H}_{19}^n(\lambda,0)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{19}^n(\lambda,1)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , where  $n\in\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  is the number of parties chosen by the adversary.

*Proof.* The lemma follows by simply observing that the distribution of the shares  $(\sigma_u)_{u \in \mathcal{U}}$  where  $\mathcal{U} = \bigcup_{q \in [q_{\text{max}}]} \mathcal{U}_q$  is now independent of the message.

### A.4 Proof of Theorem 7

<span id="page-52-0"></span>Proof. Let  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$  and  $\mathcal{I} = \{i_1, i_2, \dots, n\} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}}$ , i.e.,  $W_{\mathcal{I}} = \sum_{i \in \mathcal{I}} w_i \geq t_n$  and  $\max(\mathcal{I}) = n$ . Let us show  $(K'_n)^{-1} \cdot K_n \cdot \mu = \mu$ . We have that  $K_n = \mathsf{Lagrange}(x_{n,0}, \{\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, n | | t_n | | (2^{\lambda} - j))\}_{j \in [0,t_n)}, \{\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n | | t_n | | (2^{\lambda} - j))\}_{j \in [0,t_n)})$ , with  $x_{n,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n | | t_n | | 0)$ . Each party  $i \in \mathcal{I}$  holds  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , where  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ , with  $K_i = f_i(x_{i,0})$ ,  $\widetilde{M}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{M\mathsf{fw-share}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M\mathsf{fw-share}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_i)$  with  $M_i$  equal to  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_p, W_{i-1}, 0, w_i, i, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, \bot, 0, 0, 0](\cdot, \cdot, \cdot)$  for  $W_i = \sum_{j \in [i]} w_j$  and  $W_0 = 0$ , and  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i | | t_i | | 0)$ . During reconstruction, for each party  $i \in \mathcal{I}$  and for each  $q_i \in [w_i]$  we run the obfuscated program  $(x_{i,q_i}, \mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i}) = \widetilde{M}_i(n,t_n,q_i)$ . By correctness of  $\mathsf{Obf}$ , this outputs the values generated by

$$M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W, W^*, w_i, i, \mathsf{pos}, t^*, x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, l^*, q_1^*, q_2^*](k, t, q)$$

{53}------------------------------------------------

which runs the code in Figure 2 and has hardcoded values:  $K_f \stackrel{*}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$ ,  $K_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), K_p' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), K_{p,i} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}), W = W_{i-1}, W^* = 0,$  $w_i = w_i, i = i, pos = t^* = x_1 = x_2 = 0, v_2 = \bot, l^* = q_1^* = q_2^* = 0.$  Clearly  $n \geq i, t_n > 0$  and  $0 < q \leq w_i$ . Since n > 0 and  $t_n > 0$ , the circuit jumps to computing for every  $j \in [0, t_n)$  the evaluations  $eval[j] = Eval(K_f, n||t_n||(2^{\lambda} - j))$ and the points  $[j] = \text{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||(2^{\lambda} - j))$ . Finally the circuit computes Lagrange $(x_{i,q_i}, \{\text{eval}[j]\}_{j \in [0,t_n)}, \{\text{points}[j]\}_{j \in [0,t_n)}), \text{ where } x_{i,q_i} = \text{Eval}(K_{p,i}, n || t_n || t_n || t_n || || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_n || t_$  $(W_{i-1}+q_i)$ ). Hence, for every party  $i\in\mathcal{I}$  and for every  $q_i\in[w_i]$ , the parties obtain  $\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i} = f_n(x_{i,q_i})$ , and since  $\mathcal{I} \in \hat{\mathcal{A}}^\mathsf{fw-ethr}$ , we are guaranteed that parties collectively have at least  $t_n$  shares  $(\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i})_{i\in\mathcal{I},q_i\in[w_i]}$ . Thus, parties can compute  $K'_n = \mathsf{Lagrange}(x_{n,0}, (\mathsf{sh}_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]}, (x_{i,q_i})_{i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]})$ , which is exactly  $f_n(x_{n,0})$  whenever the interpolation denominators  $\{points[j]\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$  (used during the computation of the parties' shares) and  $(x_{i,q_i})_{i\in\mathcal{I},q_i\in[w_i]}$  (used during the reconstruction of  $K'_n$ ) are all nonzero, 13 i.e., no collision generated by the PPRF evaluation indexed by keys  $\{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}}$ . Once,  $f_n(x_{n,0})$  is computed, it is easy to see that  $K'_n = f_n(x_{n,0}) = f_n(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, n||t_n||0)) = K_n$  and  $(K'_n)^{-1} \cdot K_n \cdot \mu = \mu$ . Hence, to concludes the proof it is sufficient to show that the PPRFs (indexed by  $\{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}}$ ) do not generate collisions on distinct inputs, except with negligible probability. Let us consider the set of PPRF inputs that appear in the reconstruction:

- the  $t_n$  interpolation base points:  $\alpha_j := \{n||t_n||(2^{\lambda} j)\}$  for  $j \in [0, t_n)$ . Note that these points are fed to the PPRF indexed by  $K_p$ ;
- the share x-coordinates of the parties in the authorized subset  $\mathcal{I}$ :  $\beta_{i,q_i} := \{n||t_n||(W_{i-1}+q_i)\}$  for  $i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]$ . Note that each  $\beta_{i,q_i}$  is fed to the PPRF indexed by  $K_{p,i}$ .

We note that the PPRF inputs  $n||t_n||0$  will never collide with neither  $\alpha_j$  for any  $j \in [0, t_n)$  (since by assumption  $t_n = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ ) or with  $\beta_{i,q_i}$  since  $W_{i-1} \geq 0$  and  $q_i > 0$  for every  $i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]$ .

Let  $\mathcal{Q} := \{\alpha_j : j \in [0, t_n)\} \cup \{\beta_{i, q_i} : i \in \mathcal{I}, q_i \in [w_i]\}$ . Notice  $|\mathcal{Q}| = t_n + \sum_{i \in \mathcal{I}} w_i \leq t_n + W = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ . For any pair of functions  $G_K : \{0, 1\}^* \to \mathbb{Z}_p$ , let us define the event:

$$\mathsf{Bad}(G_K, G_{K^*}) := [\exists u, v \in \mathcal{Q} \mid u \neq v \land G_K(u) = G_{K^*}(v)].^{14}$$

We observe that:

- In the real world,  $G_K(\cdot) = \mathsf{Eval}(K, \cdot)$  for  $K \in \{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}}$ ;

<span id="page-53-0"></span>It suffices that the interpolation denominators be pairwise distinct within each respective set, i.e., no collisions occur among the elements of  $\{\text{points}[j]\}_{j\in[0,t_n)}$  and none among the elements of  $(x_{i,q_i})_{i\in\mathcal{I},\,q_i\in[w_i]}$ . Collisions between the two sets do not affect correctness, as they are never used jointly in a single interpolation. However, for simplicity, we assume the stronger condition that the two sets are mutually disjoint, which simplifies the proof.

<span id="page-53-1"></span>Note that we do not define a collision event when  $K \neq K^*$  but u = v, since this case is not relevant to our setting. Indeed, our construction never evaluates two different PPRFs on the same input  $u \in \mathcal{Q}$ .

{54}------------------------------------------------

– In the ideal world,  $G_K(\cdot) = R(\cdot)$  for an uniform random function and every  $K \in \{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}}$ .

In order to prove that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))]$  is negligible for every  $(K,K^*)\in (\{K_p\}\cup\{K_{p,i}\}_{i\in\mathcal{I}})^2$  (i.e., the PPRF indexed by K have collision with the PPRF indexed by  $K^*$  with negligible probability),  $^{15}$  we can build a PPRF PPT distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}^{\neq}$  for the case  $K\neq K^*$ , and a distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}^{=}$  for the case  $K=K^*$ .

If  $K \neq K^*$ , the distinguisher  $\mathsf{D}^{\neq}$  proceeds as follows:

- 1. Compute Q from  $(\mathcal{I}, \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}}, t_n)$ ;
- 2. Sample  $K^* \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda});$
- 3. For every  $u \in \mathcal{Q}$ , query the PPRF oracle  $\mathcal{O}(\cdot)$  and store  $z_u = \mathcal{O}(u)$ ;
- 4. For every  $u \in \mathcal{Q}$ , compute  $z_u^* = \mathsf{Eval}(K^*, u)$  and store  $z_u^*$ ;
- 5. If there exists  $u, v \in \mathcal{Q}$  with  $z_u = z_v^*$  and  $u \neq v$ , it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

That is,  $\mathsf{D}^{\neq}$  outputs 1 iff  $\mathsf{Bad}(\mathcal{O}(\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))$  holds. Let Real denote the experiment where  $\mathcal{O}(\cdot) = \mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot)$  and Rand denote the experiment where  $\mathcal{O}(\cdot) = R(\cdot)$ . Then, by construction

$$\Pr[\mathsf{D}^{\neq,\mathsf{Real}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))],$$

and

$$\Pr[\mathsf{D}^{\neq,\mathsf{Rand}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(R(\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))].$$

Therefore  $D^{\neq}$ 's PPRF distinguishing advantage is exactly:

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{D}^{\neq},\mathsf{PPRF}} := |\Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))] - \Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(R(\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))]|.$$

By applying the union bound, using the fact that  $R(\cdot)$  outputs random elements from  $\mathbb{F}_p$  with prime p of size  $\lambda+1$ , and that  $|\mathcal{Q}| \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ , we conclude that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(R(\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))]$  is negligible. Hence, if we assume towards contradiction that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,\cdot))]$  is not negligible, we would have that  $\mathsf{D}^{\neq}$  is a non-negligible PPRF distinguisher against  $\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot)$ .

On the other hand, if  $K = K^*$ , the distinguisher  $D^=$  proceeds as follows:

- 1. Compute  $\mathcal{Q}$  from  $(\mathcal{I}, \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{fw-ethr}}, t_n)$ .
- 2. For every  $u \in \mathcal{Q}$ , query the PPRF oracle  $\mathcal{O}(\cdot)$  and store  $z_u = \mathcal{O}(u)$ ;
- 3. If there exists  $u, v \in \mathcal{Q}$  with  $z_u = z_v$  and  $u \neq v$ , it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

Using a similar argument to that used for the case  $K \neq K^*$ , we conclude that:

$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathsf{D}^=,\mathsf{PPRF}} := |\Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot),\mathsf{Eval}(K,\cdot))] - \Pr[\mathsf{Bad}(R(\cdot),R(\cdot))]| \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-54-0"></span>Observe that the pairs of PPRF keys  $(K, K^*) \in (\{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}})^2$  are polynomial in the security parameters since  $|\mathcal{I}| \leq t_n \leq n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

{55}------------------------------------------------

#### Proof of Theorem 8 $\mathbf{A.5}$

<span id="page-55-0"></span>*Proof.* We need to prove that the size of each share  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{ct}_i, M_i, x_{i,0})$  is  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log W_i)$ .

First, we have that  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$  and  $x_{i,0} \in \mathbb{F}_p$ . Hence,  $|\mathsf{ct}_i| = |x_{i,0}| = \log(p) = 1$  $\log \lambda + 1 = O(\lambda)$ . To conclude the proof, it remains to show that  $|M_i|$  is in  $poly(\lambda, \log W_i)$ .

Recall that  $\widetilde{M}_i$  is computed as  $\widetilde{M}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Obf}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}}, t_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, M_i)$  with

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,i}, W_{i-1}, 0, w_i, i, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, \bot, 0, 0].$$

By the succinctness and efficiency requirements on  $\mathsf{Obf},\ |\widetilde{M}_i|$  is bounded by  $\mathsf{poly}(|M_p^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}|, \log t_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \lambda), \text{ where:}$ 

- $-|M_p^{\text{fw-share}}|$  is the description size of the Turing Machine;
- $-t_{M^{\mathrm{fw-share}}}^{\mathrm{max}}$  is the maximum runtime of the Turing Machine;  $-\ell_{M^{\mathrm{fw-share}}}^{\mathrm{max}}$  is the maximum input size of the Turing Machine.

According to Figure 2, we have  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} = 2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + |w| \text{ where } O(\log \lambda) = |w|.$ Below, we measure the remaining two parameters.

Regarding the maximum runtime  $t_{M^{\text{fw}-\text{share}}}^{\text{max}}$ :

- Comparisons with  $i, 0, w_i, pos, t^*, q_1^*, q_2^*$  can be executed in time  $poly(suplog(\lambda), q_1^*, q_2^*)$ |w|) = poly(suplog( $\lambda$ ));
- Eval $(K_f,\cdot)$ , Eval $(K_p,\cdot)$ , Eval $(K_p,\cdot)$ , and Eval $(K_{p,i},\cdot)$  can all be executed in  $(2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)).$
- Since  $l^* \leq W$  and  $|W| \leq \text{suplog}(\lambda)$  (recall the maximum weight size is  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ , the first while-loop (line 10) has runtime at most  $2^{\operatorname{suplog}(\lambda)}$ .  $poly(\lambda, suplog(\lambda));$
- Since  $t \leq t_n \leq W$  (recall the maximum weight size is  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ ), the second while-loop (line 18) has runtime  $2^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)} \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda))$ ;
- Since  $t \leq t_n \leq W$  (recall the maximum weight size is  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ ), the last while-loop (line 23) has runtime in  $(2^{2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda));$
- Modular arithmetic in  $\mathbb{F}_p$  can be executed in time  $\operatorname{poly}(\log p) = \operatorname{poly}(\lambda)$  since p is a prime of  $\lambda + 1$  bits.

Hence, the maximum runtime is bounded by

$$t_{M^{\mathsf{fw-share}}}^{\mathsf{max}} = O\left(2^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}\right) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)).$$

Regarding the description size  $|M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}|$ , we start by observing that, as described in Construction 5.1, the sizes of the hardwired values (which are part of the description of the Turing Machine) are the following:

- $\begin{array}{l} \ |K_f| = |K_p| = |K_p'| = |K_{p,i}| = |\mathsf{KeyGen}(1^\lambda)| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda); \\ \ |W| = |W^*| = |t^*| = |i| = |l^*| = |q_1^*| = |q_2^*| = \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda); \end{array}$
- $-|w_i| = |w| = O(\log \lambda);$
- $-|x_1|=|v_1|=|x_2|=|v_2|=\log p=\log(\lambda+1)$  since those values belong to  $\mathbb{F}_p$ .

{56}------------------------------------------------

Then, the computation performed by the Turing Machine can be described using the following size:

- Comparisons with  $i, 0, w_i, pos, t^*, q_1^*, q_2^*$  can be described in size  $poly(suplog(\lambda))$ .
- $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, \cdot), \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, \cdot), \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', \cdot), \text{ and } \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,i}, \cdot) \text{ can all be described in } (2 \cdot \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \lambda) \cdot \mathsf{poly}(\lambda) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda));$
- Since  $l^* \leq W$ , the first while-loop (line 10) has description size  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) + \mathsf{poly}(\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda), \lambda)$ ;
- Since  $t \leq t_n \leq W$ , the second while-loop (line 18) has description size  $suplog(\lambda) + poly(suplog(\lambda), \lambda)$ ;
- Since  $t \leq t_n \leq W$ , the while-loop (line 23) can be described in size  $2 \cdot \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda) + \operatorname{poly}(\lambda, \operatorname{suplog}(\lambda))$ ;
- Modular arithmetic in  $\mathbb{F}_p$  can be described in size  $\mathsf{poly}(\log p) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .

We conclude that the description size is bounded by

$$|M_p^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)).$$

By combining the bounds of  $|M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}|$ ,  $t_{M^{\mathsf{fw-share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$ , and  $\ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw-share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}$ , we conclude:

$$\begin{split} |\widetilde{M}_i| &= \mathsf{poly}(|M_p^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}|, \log t_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \ell_{M^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}}^{\mathsf{max}}, \lambda) \\ &= \mathsf{poly}(\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)), \log(O(2^{\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)}) \cdot \\ &\quad \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda))), \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)), \lambda) \\ &= \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)). \end{split}$$

Finally, since  $i \in [n]$  for an apriori unknown  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  (thus  $\log i = O(\log \lambda)$ ), each weight is of size  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$  (thus  $|W_i| = |\sum_{j \in [i]} w_j| \le |i \cdot w| \in \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$ ), and  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda) = \log^c(\lambda)$  for constant c > 1, and all  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$  values are chosen so as to allow the Turing machine to perform its computation correctly for every pair  $(k, t, q_i)$  whose values can depend on n (i.e., worst-case size is  $O(\log n)$ ), for an apriori unknown value  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ , we can rewrite the equation above as follows:

$$|\widetilde{M}_i| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log W_i) \text{ where } i \in [n].$$

This concludes the proof.

### A.6 Proof of Theorem 9

<span id="page-56-0"></span>Restatement of Theorem 9. If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition 9) and PPRF is secure (Definition 2), then the scheme ESS scheme of Construction 5.1, for the evolving threshold access structure with fixed weights  $\hat{A}^{\text{fw-ethr}}$  with weights of size at most  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ , is computationally private in the adaptive setting (Definition 15).

{57}------------------------------------------------

Proof. Let  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  be the two messages chosen by the adversary A in the game defining the adaptive computational privacy of SS,  $G_{\text{SS,A}}^{\text{priv}}(\lambda, b)$ . W.l.o.g. we assume that on each adversary's oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\text{share}}(n_g, \mathcal{U})$ ,  $|\mathcal{U}| \leq 1$ . Given a party  $i^*$ , we denote as  $\mathcal{Q} = (q_1, \ldots, q_m)$  the subsequence of oracle queries made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\text{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$ , where each query  $q_j$  has parameters  $(n_j, z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ . Moreover, we let  $W_{z_j}^* = \sum_{k=1}^j w_{z_k}$  be the sum of the weights of the parties requested in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , namely only those where  $z_j \leq i^*$ , up to (and including) the query in which party  $z_j$  is requested (with  $W_0^* = 0$ ).

Consider the following hybrid experiments.

 $\mathbf{H}_{0}(\lambda, b)$ : This experiment is identical to  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{A}}^{\mathsf{priv}}(\lambda, b)$ 

 $\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^{*}-1}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows. We change the machine used to generate  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{j}}$  so that, on input  $(k, t, q) = (i^{*}, t_{i^{*}}, \cdot)$ ,  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{j}}$  enters the if at line 9 in Figure 2. Moreover we set  $W^{*} = W_{z_{j-1}}^{*}$ . In particular, the machine  $M_{p}^{\mathsf{fw-share}}$  we use to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{j}}$  is replaced by  $M_{0}$  instead of  $M_{1}$  where:

 $-\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^{*},j^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)$  (with  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^{*},-1}(\lambda,b) = \mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ ), except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows.  $-\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}}^{*})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular the evaluation  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_{f},i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda}-j^{*}))$  is replaced by a random point  $r_{i^{*},j^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^{*}}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^{*}}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

{60}------------------------------------------------

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_{j-1}}^*$  and we define  $\operatorname{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = f_{i^*}(\operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_j-1}+w^*)))$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  (as  $v_1$ ) consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $v_2 = r_{i^*,j^*}$ .
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = \tilde{i}^*$ , we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}}^{*})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^{*}} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p},i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda}-j^{*}))$  is replaced by a random point  $s_{i^{*},j^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^{*}}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^{*}}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ s_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_{j-1}}^*$ , and we define  $\operatorname{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = f_{i^*}(\operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_j-1}+w^*))$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  (as  $v_1$ ) consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $x_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $x_2 = s_{i^*,j^*}$ .
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}}^{*})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular, the challenger samples a random point  $r_{i^{*},j^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$  that will be interpreted as follows:

{61}------------------------------------------------

- If  $j^* = 0$ :  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is interpreted as the key  $K_{i^*}$  (instead of computing it as Lagrange interpolation in  $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$ );
- Otherwise,  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is interpreted as  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  (as  $v_1$ ) computed when we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following

Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j = j^* = 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p, z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_j - 1} + w^*)) \text{ if } j = j^* \neq 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W^*_{z_{j-1}} < j^* \le W^*_{z_j}$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W^*_{z_{j-1}}$ , and we change the value  $v_1$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  to the randomly sampled  $\operatorname{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$ .
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 x_m}{x_j x_m}$ ., where we recall the  $x_2 = s_{i^*,j^*}$  from the previous hybrid.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{7}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}}^{*})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to all the queries as follows. For the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , when we reach the query  $q_{j}$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^{*} < j^{*} \leq W_{z_{j}}^{*}$  (note that no such query exists when  $j^{*} = 0$ , in that case we can assume j = 0, so that t > j for every query  $q_{t} \in \mathcal{Q}$ ), we denote  $w^{*} = j^{*} - W_{z_{j-1}}^{*}$  and for every query  $q_{t} \in \mathcal{Q}$  we replace the machine  $M_{p}^{\mathsf{fw-share}}$  used to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z_{t}}$  by  $M_{0}$  instead of  $M_{1}$  where:

 $-\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^{*} \in [0,t_{i^{*}}^{*})$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{8}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular, the point

$$x_{j^*} = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j^* = 0\\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p, z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || W_{z_j - 1} + w^*) \text{ otherwise} \end{cases}$$

(where  $z_j$  is the party requested at the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$ ) is replaced by a random point  $x_{j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ x_{j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

where  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is the random point sampled in  $\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and interpreted as  $K_{i^*}$  if  $j^*=0$  and  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  otherwise. As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal Q$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_j}^*$  and we define  $x_1$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  consistently as  $x_{j^*}$ ;
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we modify the share  $\sigma_{i^*}$  to include  $x_{i^*,0} = x_{j^*}$  rather than  $\text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ .

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in [0,t_{i^*}^*)$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is replaced by  $x_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*) \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}.$$

{64}------------------------------------------------

where  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is the random point sampled in  $\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and interpreted as  $K_{i^*}$  if  $j^*=0$  and  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  otherwise. As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal Q$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_j}^*$  and we define  $x_1$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  consistently as  $x_{j^*}$ ;
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we modify the share  $\sigma_{i^*}$  to include  $x_{i^*,0} = \text{Eval}(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$  rather than  $x_{j^*}$ .

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in [0,t_{i^*}^*)$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . $$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_j}^*$  and we define  $v_1$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  consistently as  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*)$ ;
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in [0,t_{i^*}^*)$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to all the queries as follows. With:

- $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*),$

- $x_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 x_m}{x_j x_m}$ , with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

 $-\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b),$ except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $y_{j^*} = \text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*)$  is replaced by  $y_{j^*} = r_{i^*, j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

{69}------------------------------------------------

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query q<sub>j</sub> such that W<sub>z<sub>j-1</sub></sub>\* < j\* ≤ W<sub>z<sub>j</sub></sub>\* (note that no such query exists for j\* = 0), we denote w\* = j\* W<sub>z<sub>j</sub></sub>\* and we define v<sub>1</sub> to be hardcoded into M<sub>z<sub>j</sub></sub> consistently as r<sub>i\*,j\*</sub>;
  For all the queries q<sub>t</sub> with t ≥ j (or for all the queries if j\* = 0), we change
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we set  $K_{i^*} = r_{i^*,j^*}$ . For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.
- $-\mathbf{H}_{20}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  is replaced by  $x_{j^*} = s_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ s_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_j}^*$  and we define  $x_1$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  consistently as  $s_{i^*,j^*}$ ;
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we modify the share  $\sigma_{i^*}$  to include  $x_{i^*,0} = s_{i^*,j^*}$  rather than  $\text{Eval}(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ .

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{20}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^*} = s_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is replaced by:

$$x_{j^*} = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j^* = 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p, z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_j - 1} + w^*)) \text{ otherwise} \end{cases}$$

{70}------------------------------------------------

(where  $z_j$  is the party queries at the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$ ). Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ x_{j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in Q as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_j}^*$  and we define  $x_1$  to be hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  consistently as  $x_{j^*}$ ;
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial. In particular:

$$v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$$

• If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we modify the share  $\sigma_{i^*}$  to include  $x_{i^*,0} = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  rather than  $s_{i^*,j^*}$ . For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  be-

haves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

 $-\mathbf{H}_{22}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to all the queries as follows.
