-  $\mathbf{H}_{24}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the challenger samples  $r_{i^*,j^*}, s_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j [0, j^*) \\ s_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows:

- When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W^*_{z_{j-1}} < j^* \le W^*_{z_j}$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* W^*_{z_{j-1}}$ , and we change the value  $v_1$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  to  $v_1 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_1-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$ , where
  - we recall  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_{p,z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_j-1} + w^*))$  from hybrid  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda, b)$ .
- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the values  $x_2, v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $v_2 = r_{i^*,j^*}$  and  $x_2 = s_{i^*,j^*}$ .
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial. In particular,

$$K_{i^*} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0) - x_m}{x_j - x_m}.$$

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{25}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{24}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^*} = s_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is replaced by  $x_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

{73}------------------------------------------------

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal Q$  as follows:

• When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* - W_{z_{j-1}}^*$ , and we change the value  $v_1$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  to  $v_1 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_1-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$ , where

we recall  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_{p,z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_j-1} + w^*))$  from hybrid  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda, b)$ .

- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $x_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $x_2 = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*))$ .
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{26}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{25}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the evaluation  $y_{j^*} = r_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is replaced by  $y_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

As a consequence, we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal Q$  as follows:

• When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W^*_{z_{j-1}} < j^* \le W^*_{z_j}$  (note that no such query exists for  $j^* = 0$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* - W^*_{z_{j-1}}$ , and we change the value  $v_1$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  to  $v_1 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_i^*-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \ne j}}^{t_i^*-1} \frac{x_1 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$ , where

we recall  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_{p,z_j}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_j-1} + w^*))$  from hybrid  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda, b)$ .

- For all the queries  $q_t$  with  $t \geq j$  (or for all the queries if  $j^* = 0$ ), we change the value  $v_2$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z_t}$  to  $v_2 = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*))$ .
- If  $j^* = 0$  and we reach a query  $q_t$  such that  $z_t = i^*$ , we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

For all remaining queries, namely those with  $z_j > i^*$ , the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  behaves exactly as in the previous hybrid.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{27}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{26}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to all the queries as follows. For the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , when we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists when  $j^* = 0$ , in that case we can assume j = 0, so that t > j for every query  $q_t \in \mathcal{Q}$ ), we denote

-  $\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t^*_{i^*},0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{27}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows. When we reach the query  $q_j$  such that  $W^*_{z_{j-1}} < j^* \leq W^*_{z_j}$  (note that no such query exists when  $j^* = 0$ , in that case we can assume j = 0, so that t > j for every query  $q_t \in \mathcal{Q}$ ), we denote  $w^* = j^* - W^*_{z_{j-1}}$  and we change the machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}$  used to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  so that  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  no longer enters the if at line 5, namely, on input  $(k,t,q) = (i^*,t_{i^*},w^*)$ , the machine behaves normally rather than outputting the explicitly hardwired value  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_i^*}$ . Hence, we replace the machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}$  used to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  by  $M_0$  instead of  $M_1$  where:

 $\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^*}(\lambda, b)$  for  $i^* \in [\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*,0}(\lambda, b)$ , except that we change the answers of the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot, \cdot)$  to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$  as follows. Moreover we set  $W^* = 0$ . In particular, the machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{fw}-\mathsf{share}}$  we use to compute  $\widetilde{M}_{z_j}$  is replaced by  $M_0$  instead of  $M_1$  where:

<span id="page-75-0"></span>**Lemma 22.** For every  $i^* \in [\operatorname{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The proof uses the hybrid argument. Let  $Q = (q_1, \ldots, q_m)$  be the subsequence of oracle queries made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\sf share}(\cdot, \cdot)$ , where each query  $q_j$  has parameters  $(n_j, z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ ; for every  $z \in [0, |\mathcal{Q}|]$ , let  $\boldsymbol{H}_1^{i^*, z}(\lambda, b)$  be the experiment where we change the first z answers in  $\mathcal{Q}$ .

Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},|\mathcal{Q}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} = \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $z\in[|\mathcal{Q}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z^{*}}$  with  $z^{*}$  being the party corrupted in the z-th query in  $\mathcal{Q}$ .

{76}------------------------------------------------

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input (k, t, q) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z^*$ , t > 0, and  $0 < q \leq w_{z^*}$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 cases:

- $-k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ : In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w_{z^*}$  in  $M_0$  we do not enter any different branch of code compared to  $M_1$ , since no condition is fully satisfied, i.e.,  $q \ne q_1^*$  and  $q > q_2^*$  (recall that  $q_1^* = q_2^* = 0$ ); moreover  $j \ge l^*$  (recall that  $l^* = 0$ ), and  $v_2 = \bot$ . So both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output (Eval $(K_{z^*}, k||t||(W+q)), S$ ).
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z^*},k||t||(W+q)),S)$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,z}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-76-0"></span>**Lemma 23.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in [0, t_{i^*}), \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*, j^* - 1}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^{*},j^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z_{j}}$  with  $z_{j}$  being the party queried in the query  $q_{j}$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^{*} < j^{*} \leq W_{z_{j}}^{*}$ . When  $j^{*} = 0$ , no such query exists, hence  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^{*},-1} \equiv \mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}} \equiv \mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},0}$ . When  $j^{*} > 0$ , the lemma follows by security of Obf.

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input (k, t, q) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z_j$ , t > 0, and  $0 < q \leq w_{z_j}$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 3 cases:

 $-k=i^*$ ,  $t=t_{i^*}$ , and  $q=w^*$ : In this case, in  $M_0$  we output  $(x_1,v_1)$ , which corresponds to  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||W_{z_j-1}+w^*))$ ,  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$ , while in  $M_1$  we output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},k||t||(W_{z_j-1}+q)),S)$ . Notice that  $\mathsf{sh}_{z_j,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  and S are computed exactly at the same way, i.e., as the Lagrange interpolation in  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_j-1}+w^*))$  of a degree  $t_{i^*}-1$  polynomial evaluated at the  $t_{i^*}$  distinct points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

for all  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ .

 $-k = i^*, t = t_{i^*}, \text{ and } q \leq w^* - 1$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', k||t||(W_{z_{j-1}}^* + q)), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, k||t||(W_{z_{j-1}}^* + q)))$ .

{77}------------------------------------------------

 $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$  or  $q > w^*$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\text{Eval}(K_{p,z_i},k||t||(W_{z_i-1}+q)),S)$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\{\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-77-0"></span>**Lemma 24.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

Proof. The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every query  $q \in [q_{\mathsf{max}}]$ , where  $q_{\mathsf{max}}$  is the maximum number of queries made by the adversary, we let  $\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares for the first q queries. Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q_{\mathsf{max}}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $q \in [q_{\mathsf{max}}]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the party queried in the q-th query.

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Firstly, we analyse the case where the q-th query is in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , namely,  $z \leq i^*$ . We let the q-th query be  $q_x \in \mathcal{Q}$ , and the query  $q_j \in \mathcal{Q}$  be the query such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists when  $j^* = 0$ , in that case we can assume j = 0, so that t > j for every query  $q_t \in \mathcal{Q}$ ). In this case, assuming that there is an input (k, t, q) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z_x$ , t > 0, and  $0 < q \leq w_{z_x}$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- $k = i^* \text{ and } t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If x < j: In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w_{z_x}$  neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  are never called, as both circuits output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q))$ . Notice that  $2^{\lambda} j^*$  and  $W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q$  never intersect, since by assumption  $W_n = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ .
  - If x = j: In this case, neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*))$  are never called, as both circuits output:  $(x_1, v_1)$  for  $q = w^*$ ,
    - \*  $(\operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)), \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)))$  for  $0 < q < w^*$ ,
    - \* (Eval $(K_{p,z_x}, k||t||(W_{z_x-1}+q)), S$ ) for  $w^* < q \le w_{z_x}$ , where Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  are already set within  $x_2$  and  $x_2$ ;
  - If x > j: In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\text{Eval}(K_{p,z_x}, k||t||(W_{z_x-1}+q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  or  $\text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ , whose values are already set within  $x_2$  and  $x_2$ ;
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_x},k||t||(W_{z_x-1}+q)),S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ .

{78}------------------------------------------------

Secondly, we analyse the case where the q-th query is not in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , namely,  $z > i^*$ . In this case, for every input where  $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$  (i.e., the inputs corresponding to the point where  $K_f$  and  $K_p$  have been punctured), both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will abort because z > k.

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-78-0"></span>**Lemma 25.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the pseudorandomness at punctured points of PPRF (Definition 2) as follows:

- The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{SS,D}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary D.
- The reduction sends to the PPRF security game the point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*)$  and receives  $K^* = \text{Punc}(K, \{i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*)\})$  and either a uniform value  $\bar{u} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  or the value  $\bar{u} = \text{Eval}(K, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*))$ , where K is the PPRF key generated by the PPRF challenger.
- The reduction computes  $K_{p,*} = \mathsf{Punc}(K_p, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | (2^{\lambda} j^*)\})$ , and  $K_p' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- At each oracle query  $q_t$  to  $\mathcal{O}_{\sf share}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , on input  $(n_t,z_t)$ :
  - If  $q_t \notin \mathcal{Q}$ : the reduction computes  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,*}, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ ,  $K_{z_t} = \operatorname{Lagrange}(x_{z_t,0}, \{\operatorname{Eval}(K_*, z_t || t_{z_t} || (2^{\lambda} j))\}_{j \in [0,t_{z_t})}, \{\operatorname{Eval}(K_p, z_t || t_{z_t} || (2^{\lambda} j))\}_{j \in [0,t_{z_t})})$ , and  $K_{p,z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \operatorname{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$  and sets:

$$M_{z_t} = M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, 0, w_{z_t}, z_t, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, \bot, 0, 0, 0],$$

and 
$$\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$$
. Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$ .

- If  $q_t \in \mathcal{Q}$ :
  - \* If  $W_{z_t}^* < j^*$ : the reduction sets  $M_{z_t} = M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_{t-1}}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, W_{z_t}^*, 0, w_{z_t}]$ . Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $\text{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_{z_t,0} = \text{Eval}(K_{p,*}, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , it sets  $K_{z_t} = \text{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ ,  $\text{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ , and  $x_{z_t,0} = \text{Eval}(K_p', z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\text{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$ .
  - \* If  $W_{z_{t-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_t}^*$ : we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_{t-1}}^*$ , and the reduction computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique polynomial of degree  $t_{i^*} 1$  obtained by interpolating the values:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || j), \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \bar{u} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

{79}------------------------------------------------

at the points

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Then, the reduction proceeds by setting:

$$\begin{split} x_1 &= \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_t}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_t-1} + w^*)), \\ \mathsf{sh}_{z_t,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} &= \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_t}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_t-1} + w^*)) - x_m}{x_j - x_m}, \\ x_2 &= \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j^*)), \end{split}$$

and  $v_2 = \bar{u}$ .

Then, the reduction sets

$$\begin{split} M_{z_t} &= M_p^{\mathsf{fw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, \\ & x_1, \mathsf{sh}_{z_t, w^*}^{t_{i^*}}, x_2, v_2, j^*, w^*, w^* - 1]. \end{split}$$

Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,*}, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , it set  $K_{z_t} = \operatorname{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ ,  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ , and  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K'_p, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M}_{z_t}, x_{z_t,0})$ .

\* For all the other queries in Q, the reduction sets

$$\begin{split} M_{z_t} &= M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, \\ & 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0], \end{split}$$

where  $x_2$  and  $v_2$  are those computed at the previous step. Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,*}, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , if  $j^* = 0$  the reduction computes  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,*}, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$  and  $K_{z_t} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \\ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_{z_t,0}-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$ , (where  $y_j$  and  $x_j$  are those defined at the previous step), otherwise (if  $j^* \neq 0$ ) it sets  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$  and  $K_{z_t} = \operatorname{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$  and then  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$ .

- Finally, the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-79-1"></span>**Lemma 26.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_5^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

<span id="page-79-0"></span>*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_5^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 25 where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{p,*}$  and  $x_2$  (and hence  $x_{j^*}$ ) respectively (instead of  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ), while the point  $v_2$  (and hence  $y_{j^*}$ ) is randomply sampled. We omit it for brevity.

{80}------------------------------------------------

**Lemma 27.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)], j^* \in [0, t_{i^*}), and for every <math>b \in \{0, 1\}, it$ holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ .

- \* If  $W_{z_{t-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_t}^*$ : we denote  $w^* = j^* W_{z_{t-1}}^*$ , and the reduction sends to the security game of Lemma 1:
  - $n = i^*$ ;
  - $\cdot t = t_{i^*};$

$$\mathcal{I} = \{x_j \mid x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

with  $|\mathcal{I}| = t_{i^*} - 1$ ;

 $i_{t-1} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j^*));$ 

 $\cdot i^* = \text{Eval}(K_{p,z_t}, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_t-1} + w^*));$ 

$$\mathcal{Y} = \{y_j \mid y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

with  $|\mathcal{Y}| = t_{i^*} - 1$ ;

{81}------------------------------------------------

The Lemma 1 challenger randomly samples  $y_{t-1}$  and computes  $r_b$  either as a random value or as  $f(i^*) = \sum_{j=0}^{t-1} y_j \ell_j(i^*)$ , where  $\ell_j(x) = \prod_{0 \le m \le t-1} \frac{x-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$ . Then, it forwards  $r_b$  to the reduction. The reduction proceeds by setting  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_{p,z_t}, i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_t-1} + w^*))$ ,  $v_1 = r_b$ ,  $x_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \ne j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$  (where  $y_{j^*} = r_b$ ,  $x_{j^*} = x_1$ , while the values  $(y_j)_{j \in [0,t_{i^*}) \setminus \{j^*\}}$  and  $(x_j)_{j \in [0,t_{i^*}) \setminus \{j^*\}}$  are those in  $\mathcal Y$  and in  $\mathcal I$  respectively). Then, the reduction sets:

$$\begin{split} M_{z_t} &= M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, \\ & x_1, v_1, x_2, v_2, j^*, w^*, w^* - 1]. \end{split}$$

Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , it set  $K_{z_t} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ ,  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ , and  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$ .

- \* For all the other queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$ : if  $j^* = 0$ , the the reduction sends to the security game of Lemma 1:
  - $\cdot n = i^*;$
  - $t = t_{i*}$
  - $\mathcal{I} = \{ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* | |t_{i^*}| | (2^{\lambda} j)) \}_{j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*})}, \text{ with } |\mathcal{I}| = t_{i^*} 1;$
  - $i_{t-1} = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 2^{\lambda});$
  - $\cdot i^* = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0);$
  - $\mathcal{Y} = \{ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j)) \}_{j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*})}, \text{ with } |\mathcal{Y}| = t_{i^*} 1;$  The Lemma 1 challenger randomly samples  $y_{t-1}$  and computes  $r_b$  either as a random value or as  $f(i^*) = \sum_{j=0}^{t-1} y_j \ell_j(i^*), \text{ where } \ell_j(x) = \prod_{\substack{0 \leq m \leq t-1 \\ m \neq j}} \frac{x x_m}{x_j x_m}.$  Then, it forwards  $r_b$  to the reduction. The re-

duction proceeds by setting  $x_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_i*-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m\neq j}}^{t_i*-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$  (where  $y_{j^*} = r_b, x_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ , while the values  $(y_j)_{j \in [1, t_{i^*})}$  and  $(x_j)_{j \in [1, t_{i^*})}$  are those in  $\mathcal Y$  and in  $\mathcal I$  respectively). Then, the reduction sets:

$$\begin{split} M_{z_t} &= M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, \\ & 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0]. \end{split}$$

Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $x_{z_t,0} = \text{Eval}(K_p, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$  and  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , it sets  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ ,  $K_{z_t} = r_b$ , and  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$  While if  $j^* \neq 0$ : the reduction sets

$$\begin{split} M_{z_t} &= M_p^{\text{fw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', K_{p,z_t}, W_{z_t-1}, W_{z_{t-1}}^*, w_{z_t}, z_t, i^*, t_{i^*}, \\ & 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0], \end{split}$$

{82}------------------------------------------------

where  $x_2$  and  $v_2$  are the ones set at the step where  $W_{z_{t-1}}^* < j^* \le W_{z_t}^*$ . Moreover, if  $z_t < i^*$ , the reduction sets  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, z_t || t_{z_t} || 0)$  and  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ , while if  $z_t = i^*$ , it sets  $x_{z_t,0} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ ,  $K_{z_t} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || 0)$ , and  $\operatorname{ct}_{z_t} = K_{z_t} \cdot \mu_b$ . Finally  $\sigma_{z_t} = (\operatorname{ct}_{z_t}, \widetilde{M_{z_t}}, x_{z_t,0})$ .

- Finally the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

<span id="page-82-1"></span>**Lemma 28.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf, since, as shown in Lemma 24,  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} - j^*))$  and  $\text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} - j^*))$  are never called. We omit the proof here for brevity.

<span id="page-82-0"></span>**Lemma 29.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $q \in [q_{\text{max}}]$ , where  $q_{\text{max}}$  is the maximum number of queries made by the adversary, we let  $\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares for the first q queries. Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q_{\text{max}}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $q \in [q_{\text{max}}]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ .

The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{8}^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{8}^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the party queried in the q-th query.

Firstly, we analyse the case where the q-th query is in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , namely  $z \leq i^*$ . We define  $q_j$  as the query in  $\mathcal{Q}$  such that  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^* \leq W_{z_j}^*$  (note that no such query exists when  $j^* = 0$ , in that case we can assume j = 0), and we denote  $w^* = j^* - W_{z_{j-1}}^*$ . We let the q-th query be  $q_x \in \mathcal{Q}$ .

In this case, assuming that there is an input (k, t, q) for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z_x$ , t > 0, and  $0 < q \leq w_{z_x}$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- If  $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If x < j: In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w_{z_x}$  neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  and Eval $(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  are never called, as both circuits output  $(\text{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)), \text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)))$  and for every  $q \in [w_{z_x}]$  we have that  $W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q \le W_{z_x}^* \le W_{z_{j-1}}^*$  (since x < j), and  $W_{z_{j-1}}^* < j^*$  by definition, hence  $W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q < j^*$  for every  $q \in [w_{z_x}]$ .
  - If x = j: In this case, neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  and Eval $(K'_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  are never called, as both circuits output:  $(x_1, v_1)$  for  $q = w^*$ ;

{83}------------------------------------------------

- \*  $(\text{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)), \text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)))$  for  $0 < q < w^*$ ;
- $* \; (\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_x},k||t||(W_{z_x}+q)),S) \; \text{for} \; w^* < q \leq w_{z_x}, \; \text{without ever calling} \; \mathsf{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*) \; \text{or} \; \mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*) \; \text{because} \; l^* \; \text{is equal to} \\ j^* \; (\text{hence we exit the while-loop}), \; \text{and without ever calling} \; \mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||0) \; \text{or} \; \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||W_{z_j-1}+w^*) \; \text{because} \; W_{z_x-1}+q>0 \; \text{for} \\ every \; q \in [w_{z_x}] \; \text{and} \; W_{z_j-1}+w^* < W_{z_j-1}+q \; \text{for} \; w^* < q \leq w_{z_x};$
- If x > j: In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_x},k||t||(W_{z_x-1}+q)),S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  because  $l^*$  is equal to  $j^*$ , and without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j},i^*||t_{i^*}||W_{z_j-1}+w^*)$  because  $W_{z_x-1}+q>0$  and  $K_{p,z_j}\neq K_{p,z_x}$  since x>j.
- $-k \neq i^* \text{ or } t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_x}, k||t|| (W_{z_x-1}+q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_{p,z_j}, i^*||t_{i^*}||W_{z_j-1} + w^*)$  (or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$ ).

Secondly, we analyse the case where the q-th query is not in  $\mathcal{Q}$ , namely  $z > i^*$ . In this case, for every input  $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$  (i.e., the inputs corresponding to the points where  $K_f, K_p, K_p', K_{p,z_j}$  have been punctured), both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will abort because z > k.

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus, conditioned on E (only if  $j^* > 0$ ),  $\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*,q}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-83-2"></span>**Lemma 30.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

Proof. The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||0$  if  $j^*=0$ , and  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_j-1}+w^*)$  if  $j^*>0$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 25, where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{p,*}$  and  $x_{i^*,0}$  (if  $j^*=0$ ) and as  $K_{p,z_j,*}$  and  $x_1$  (if  $j^*>0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $v_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-83-1"></span>**Lemma 31.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ ,  $j^* \in [0, t_{i^*})$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 25, where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K'_{p,*}$  and  $x_{i^*,0}$  (if  $j^*=0$ ) and as  $K'_{p,*}$  and  $x_1$  (if  $j^*>0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $v_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-83-0"></span>**Lemma 32.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in [0, t_{i^*}), \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

{84}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 25 where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{f,*}$  and  $K'_{i^*}$ (if  $j^* = 0$ ) and as  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_1$  (if  $j^* > 0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $x_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-84-1"></span>**Lemma 33.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)], j^* \in [0, t_{i^*}), and for every <math>b \in \{0, 1\}, it$ holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 29 with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

<span id="page-84-0"></span>**Lemma 34.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)], j^* \in [0, t_{i^*}), and for every <math>b \in \{0, 1\}, it$ holds that  $\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, let  $Q = (q_1, \ldots, q_m)$ be the subsequence of oracle queries made to  $\mathcal{O}_{\sf share}(\cdot,\cdot)$ , where each query  $q_i$ has parameters  $(n_j, z_j)$  with  $z_j \leq i^*$ ; for every  $z \in [0, |\mathcal{Q}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*, j^*, z}(\lambda, b)$  be the experiment where we change the first z answers to the queries in  $\mathcal{Q}$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \text{ and } \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,|\mathcal{Q}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}},$ and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $z \in [|\mathcal{Q}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z^*}$  with  $z^*$  being the party corrupted in the z-th query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}(\cdot,\cdot)$ . We let the z-th query be  $q_x \in \mathcal{Q}$ , and the query  $q_j$  be the first query such that  $W_{z_j}^* \geq j^*$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input (k, t, q) for which  $M_0, M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z_x$ , t > 0, and  $0 < q \leq w_{z_x}$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- $-k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If x < j, for any  $0 < q \le w_{z_x}$ , both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  outputs  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} ||$
  - $(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q))$ , Eval $(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q))$ ; If x = j: if  $q = w^*$ ,  $M_1$  outputs  $(x_1, v_1)$  while  $M_0$  outputs (Eval $(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{i^*} || t_{$  $(W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q))$ , Eval $(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q))$ , which are exactly the same values of  $x_1$  and  $v_1$ ; otherwise, if  $q < w^*$ , both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  outputs  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_{x-1}}^* + q)); \text{ for } w^* < 0$  $q < w_{z_x}$  the outputs are the same described in the next case;
  - If x > j:  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  differs on how they compute the  $j^*$ -th evaluation of the polynomial. In particular, in  $M_1$  we use  $x_2$  and  $v_2$ , while in  $M_0$ , since we incremented  $l^*$ , we compute the  $j^*$ -th evaluation within the while loop  $(j < l^*)$ . Notice that

$$v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$$

{85}------------------------------------------------

with 
$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$
 and 
$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Hence, in  $M_1$  the  $j^*$ -th evaluation is basically  $v_2$ , computed as Lagrange interpolation of a polynomial where  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*))$  is one of the points, while in  $M_0$ , the  $j^*$ -th evaluation is directly  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || j^*))$ . It follows that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, z_x, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_x-1} + q)), S)$  (with exactly the same S).  $-k \neq i^*$  and  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, z_x, i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z_x-1} + q)), S)$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*,z}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-85-0"></span>**Lemma 35.** For every  $i^* \in [poly(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,t_{i^*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. Indeed all the parties  $z \leq i^*$  now enter the if at line 7 in Figure 2, thus  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  is never evaluated within the machines, while for all the parties  $z > i^*$  the machines abort for an input  $(k, t, \cdot) = (i^*, t_{i^*}, \cdot)$ .

**Lemma 36.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$  and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by observing that the two hybrids differ only in the answer of  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{share}}$  on input  $(n_g, i^*)$ ; in the former hybrid  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu_b$  is a one-time-pad encryption under a uniform key  $K_{i^*}$ , while in the latter  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*}$  is sampled uniformly at random, which is identically distributed to a one-time-pad encryption.

**Lemma 37.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,t_{i^*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The proof is analogous to the one in Lemma 35.

**Lemma 38.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*, j^* - 1}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 34, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

{86}------------------------------------------------

**Lemma 39.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 33, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 40.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 32, with  $K_{i^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $K_{i^*} = \text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  inverted (if  $j^* = 0$ ), and with  $v_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $v_1 = \text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  inverted (if  $j^* > 0$ ).

**Lemma 41.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{19}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{20}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 31, with  $x_{i^*,0} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_{i^*,0} = \text{Eval}(K'_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  inverted (if  $j^* = 0$ ), and with  $x_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K'_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||j^*)$  inverted (if  $j^* > 0$ ).

**Lemma 42.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{20}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_x-1}+w^*)$  (or  $i^*||t_{i^*}||0$  if  $j^*=0$ ). The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 30 with  $x_{i^*,0}=\operatorname{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||0)$  and  $x_{i^*,0} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  inverted (if  $j^*=0$ ), and with  $x_1=\operatorname{Eval}(K_{p,z_x},i^*||t_{i^*}||(W_{z_x-1}+w^*))$  and  $x_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  inverted (if  $j^*>0$ ).

**Lemma 43.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{22}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of  $\mathsf{Obf}$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 29, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 44.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{22}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 28, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 45.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{24}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Lemma 1. The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{24}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 27. We omit it for brevity.

{87}------------------------------------------------

**Lemma 46.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{24}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{25}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 26 with  $s_{i^*,j^*}$  and  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  inverted.

**Lemma 47.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{25}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{26}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 26 with  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  and  $\text{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  inverted.

**Lemma 48.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{26}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{27}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 24, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 49.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)], j^* \in (t_{i^*}, 0], \text{ and for every } b \in \{0, 1\}, \text{ it holds that } \{\mathbf{H}_{27}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 23, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 50.** For every  $i^* \in [\text{poly}(\lambda)]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 22, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 51.**  $\{\mathbf{H}_{29}^n(\lambda,0)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{29}^n(\lambda,1)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , where  $n\in\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  is the number of parties chosen by the adversary.

*Proof.* The lemma follows by simply observing that the distribution of the shares  $(\sigma_u)_{u \in \mathcal{U}}$  where  $\mathcal{U} = \bigcup_{q \in [q_{\text{max}}]} \mathcal{U}_q$  is now independent of the message.

### A.7 Proof of Theorem 10

<span id="page-87-0"></span>*Proof.* The proof is similar to that of Theorem 7 (Appendix A.4), with the following differences:

- When constructing the set of PPRF inputs  $\mathcal{Q}$  on which we measure the probability of presenting a collision, these points must include the SSB hash  $h_n$ .
- In addition, we need to measure only the probability of a collision for a single PPRF indexed by  $K_p$  (in contrast to the proof of Theorem 7, where we consider the collision probability of any pair of PPRFs indexed by K and  $K^*$ , with  $(K, K^*) \in (\{K_p\} \cup \{K_{p,i}\}_{i \in \mathcal{I}})^2$ .

   Since there is a single PPRF indexed by  $K_p$ , it is sufficient to consider
- Since there is a single PPRF indexed by  $K_p$ , it is sufficient to consider only the case  $K = K^* = K_p$  (and the related distinguisher  $D^=$ ) described in Appendix A.4.

{88}------------------------------------------------

### A.8 Proof of Theorem 11

<span id="page-88-0"></span>*Proof.* The proof of the theorem is essentially identical to that of Theorem 8 of Construction 5.1 except that when calculating the maximum input-size  $\ell_{M^{\text{fw-share}}}^{\text{max}}$ , worst-case running time  $t_{M^{\text{dw-share}}}^{\text{max}}$ , and description size  $|M_p^{\text{dw-share}}|$  we must consider the following bounds that are implied by the efficiency and succinctness of SSB (Definition 7):

- Since p is a prime of  $(\lambda^c)$ -bits for constant c > 1, each value in  $\mathbb{F}_p$  can be represented using  $|\mathbb{F}_p| = \log(p) = \log(\lambda^c) = O(\log \lambda)$ ;
- $\ell_{\mathsf{hash}}$  and  $\ell_{\mathsf{open}}$  (hashes and openings produced by SSB) are bounded by  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, |w|, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda))$  since  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ ;
- The hardcoded value hk is of size at most  $|\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{\mathsf{block}}}, 2^{\lambda}, 1)| = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, |w| \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)) \text{ since } |w| = O(\log \lambda);^{16}$
- The runtime of Verify(hk,  $\cdot$ ,  $\cdot$ ,  $\cdot$ ) is bounded by  $poly(\lambda, log(2^{\lambda})) = poly(\lambda)$ ;
- The description of the Turing machine code for Verify(hk,  $h, i, w, \pi$ ) has description size of poly( $\lambda$ , log( $2^{\lambda}$ )) = poly( $\lambda$ ).

#### A.9 Proof of Theorem 12

<span id="page-88-1"></span>Restatement of Theorem 12. If the iO obfuscator Obf is secure (Definition 9) PPRF is secure (Definition 2), and SSB is index hiding (Definition 5) and somewhere perfectly binding (Definition 6), then the scheme ESS scheme of Construction 6.1, for the evolving threshold access structure with dynamic weights  $\hat{A}^{\text{dw-ethr}}$  with weights of size at most  $|w| = O(\log \lambda)$ , is a computationally private in the static setting (Definition 15).

*Proof.* Let n, and  $\mathcal{U} \notin \hat{\mathcal{A}}^{\mathsf{dw-ethr}}$  be, respectively, the number of parties, and the unqualified subset chosen by the adversary in the game defining the static computational privacy of  $\mathbf{G}^{\mathsf{priv}}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{A}}(\lambda,b)$ . Consider the following hybrid experiments.

 $\mathbf{H}_{0}(\lambda, b)$ : This experiment is identical to  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{A}}^{\mathsf{priv}}(\lambda, b)$ .

We define:

$$\begin{split} &-W_{k^*,i^*}^* = \sum_{\substack{z \in \mathcal{U} \\ z \leq k^*}} \mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(z), \\ &-j^* \in [0,W_{i^*,i^*}], \\ &-z^* = \begin{cases} 0 \text{ if } j^* = 0 \\ \min(u \in \mathcal{U} \mid W_{u,i^*}^* > j^*) \text{ otherwise} \\ &-w^* = j^* - W_{z^*-1,i^*}^*. \end{split}$$

<span id="page-88-2"></span>Recall that, as described in the proof of Theorem 8, the values  $\mathsf{suplog}(\lambda)$  are used to safely encode any value that depends polynomially on  $n \in \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ , for an a priori unknown value of n. This implies that  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \mathsf{suplog}(\lambda))$  can be rewritten as  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda, \log n)$ .

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Moreover, we set  $v_2 = r_{i^*,j^*}$ , and if  $j^* = 0$  we compute  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial, while if  $j^* > 0$  we compute  $\mathsf{sh}^{t_{i^*}}_{z^*,w^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

 $-\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in \mathcal{U}, j^{*} \in [0,W_{i^{*},i^{*}}^{*}]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^{*}} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p},i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||h_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda}-j^{*}))$  is replaced by random point  $s_{i^{*},j^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^{*}}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^{*}}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ s_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Moreover, we set  $x_2 = s_{i^*,j^*}$ , and if  $j^* = 0$  we compute  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial, while if  $j^* > 0$  we compute  $\mathsf{sh}^{t_{i^*}}_{z^*,w^*} = f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

- $-\mathbf{H}_{7}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^{*} \in \mathcal{U}, j^{*} \in [0,W_{i^{*},i^{*}}^{*}]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^{*}}(x)$ . In particular, the challenger samples a random point  $r_{i^{*},j^{*}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$  that will be interpreted as follows:
  - If  $j^* = 0$ :  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is interpreted as the key  $K_{i^*}$  (instead of computing it as Lagrange interpolation in  $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0)$ );
  - Otherwise,  $r_{i^*,j^*}$  is interpreted as  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  hardcoded into  $\widetilde{M}_{z^*}$  (as  $v_1$ ). Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j = j^* = 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*)) \text{ if } j = j^* \neq 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

{92}------------------------------------------------

Moreover, we set

$$v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$$

with  $y_j$  and  $x_j$  (for all  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ ) defined as above. Recall that in the previous hybrid we set  $x_2 = s_{i^*,j^*}$ .

-  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}, j^* \in [W_{i^*,i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{20}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*] \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Moreover, we set  $v_2$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial, and if  $j^* > 0$  we set  $v_1 = r_{i^*,j^*}$ , while if  $j^* = 0$  we set  $K_{i^*} = r_{i^*,j^*}$ .

-  $\mathbf{H}_{22}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}, j^* \in [W_{i^*,i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the point  $x_{j^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  is replaced by  $x_{j^*} = s_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . $$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0j^*) \\ r_{i^*, j^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Moreover we set  $x_2 = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} - j^*))$ , and if  $j^* > 0$  we set  $v_1 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_1 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$  (where we recall  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda} + y_j))$ )

 $w^*$ )) from hybrid  $\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , while if  $j^*=0$  we define  $K_{i^*}=f_{i^*}(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

 $-\overline{\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*,j^*}}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}, j^* \in [W_{i^*,i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{27}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$ . In particular, the evaluation  $y_{j^*} = r_{i^*,j^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is replaced by  $y_{j^*} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ . Specifically, the polynomial  $f_{i^*}$  is computed by interpolating the following  $t_{i^*}$  points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^\lambda - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

{100}------------------------------------------------

over

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^*, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

Moreover we set  $v_2 = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} - j^*))$ , and if  $j^* > 0$  we set  $v_1 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_1 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$  (where we recall  $x_1 = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*))$  from hybrid  $\mathbf{H}_{23}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , while if  $j^* = 0$  we define  $K_{i^*} = f_{i^*}(\operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0))$  consistently as Lagrange interpolation of the resulting polynomial.

-  $\mathbf{H}_{29}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  for  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}, j^* \in [W_{i^*,i^*}^*,0]$ : This is identical to  $\mathbf{H}_{28}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ , except that we change how the challenger computes the obfuscation  $\widetilde{M}_z$  for all the parties  $z \in \mathcal{U}$ . In particular, the machine  $M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}$  we use to compute  $\widetilde{M}_z$  for all the parties  $z \in \mathcal{U}$  is replaced by  $M_0$  instead of  $M_1$  where:
