<span id="page-101-1"></span>**Lemma 52.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{31}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$   $\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

Proof. The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $u \in [0, |\mathcal{U}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},u}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares  $\sigma_{z}$  for  $z \in \mathcal{U}|_{u}$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{31}^{i^{*}-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $u \in [|\mathcal{U}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{1}^{i^{*},u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z}$  with z being the u-th party in  $\mathcal{U}$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,  $h, z, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$  and  $0 < q \leq w$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 cases:

- $-k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ : In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w$  in  $M_0$  we do not enter any different branch of code compared to  $M_1$ , since no condition is fully satisfied, i.e.,  $q \ne q_1^*$  and  $q > q_2^*$  (recall that  $q_1^* = q_2^* = 0$ ); moreover  $j \ge l^*$  (recall that  $l^* = 0$ ), and  $v_2 = \bot$ . So both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output (Eval $(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda} + q)), S$ ).
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output (Eval $(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda}+q)), S$ ).

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_1^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{31}^{i^*-1}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-101-0"></span>**Lemma 53.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*, j^* - 1}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* First of all, we note that for  $j^* = 0$ ,  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*-1}(\lambda,b) = \mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ . For  $j^* > 0$ , the lemma follows by SSB being index hiding (Definition 5). We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the index hiding of SSB as follows:

{102}------------------------------------------------

- The reduction receives two messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1$ , an integer n and an unauthorized subset  $\mathcal{U} \notin \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{A}}^{\mathsf{priv}}(\lambda,b)$  adversary  $\mathsf{D}$ ;
- The reduction sends to the SSB challenger the integer  $2^{\lambda}$  and the indices  $i_0 = z^* 1$  and  $i_1 = z^*$ ;
- The SSB challenger samples a random bit b, runs  $hk \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}, 1^{\ell_{\mathsf{block}}}, 2^{\lambda}, i_b)$ , and returns hk to the reduction;
- The reduction proceeds computing:
  - $K_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda}),$
  - $K_p \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$
  - $K_p' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{KeyGen}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- Then, the reduction proceeds computing the shares  $(\sigma_i)_{i \in [n]}$  as follows:
  - If  $i = i^*$ : the dealer computes  $h_{i^*} = \mathsf{Hash}(\mathsf{hk}, (\mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(i))_{i \in [i^*]})$  and  $K_{i^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0)$  Then the dealer sets  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu$ . Then, if  $i^* = z^*$ , the dealer sets:

$$M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, j^*, 0, w^*-1],$$

otherwise it sets:

$$M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, j^*, 0, 0].$$

Finally, 
$$\sigma_{i^*} = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_{i^*}, \widetilde{M}_{i^*}, x_{i^*,0}), \text{ where } x_{i^*,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0).$$

• If  $i < i^*$ : the dealer sets  $\mathsf{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Then, if  $i = z^*$ , the dealer sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, j^*, 0, w^* - 1],$$

otherwise if  $i < z^*$  it sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, W_{i,i^*}^*, 0, \mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(i)],$$

otherwise if  $i > z^*$  it sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, j^*, 0, 0],$$

and finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$  where  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0)$ .

• If  $i > i^*$ : the dealer computes  $h_i = \mathsf{Hash}(\mathsf{hk}, (\mathsf{weight}_i(x))_{x \in [i]})$ , and  $K_i = f_i(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0))$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i-1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  at the points  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  for all  $j \in [0, t_i)$  and sets  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu$ . Then, the dealer sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_f, K_p, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1, i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, j^*, 0, 0],$$

and finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , where  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0)$ .

- The reduction forwards  $\{\sigma_u\}_{u\in\mathcal{U}}$  to D.
- Finally, the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

{103}------------------------------------------------

It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-103-1"></span>**Lemma 54.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* First of all, we note that for  $j^* = 0$ ,  $\mathbf{H}_2^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b) = \mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ . For  $j^* > 0$ , the lemma follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_{z^*}$  with  $z^* = \min(u \in \mathcal{U} \mid W_{u,i^*}^* > j^*)$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0, M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z^*$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,  $h, z^*, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$  and  $0 < q \leq w$ must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 3 cases:

 $-k=i^*$ ,  $t=t_{i^*}$ , and  $q=w^*$ : In this case, in  $M_0$  we output  $(x_1,v_1)$ , which corresponds to  $(\text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*)), \text{sh}_{z^*, w^*}^{t_{i^*}})$ , while in  $M_1$  we output (Eval $(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z^*\lambda}+q)), S$ ). We note that  $\mathsf{hk} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda, 1^{\ell_{\mathsf{block}}}, 2^\lambda, z^*)$ and  $h_{i^*} = \mathsf{Hash}(\mathsf{hk}, (\mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(i))_{i \in [i^*]})$  are honestly generated by the reduction and so since SSB is statistically binding, we know that  $w = w_{z^*}$ . This means that  $\mathsf{sh}^{t_{i^*}}_{z^*,w^*}$  and S are computed exactly at the same way, i.e., as the Lagrange interpolation in  $\text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*))$  of a degree  $t_{i^*} - 1$ polynomial evaluated at the  $t_{i^*}$  distinct points:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j < j^* \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \geq j^* \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j < j^* \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \geq j^* \end{cases}$$

for  $j \in [0, t_{i^*})$ .

- $-k=i^*, t=t_{i^*}, \text{ and } q \leq w^*-1$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output
- $(\text{Eval}(K'_p, k||t||h||(W^*_{z^*-1,i^*}+q)), \text{Eval}(K_f, k||t||h||(W^*_{z^*-1,i^*}+q))).$   $k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$  or  $q > w^*$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z^*\lambda} + q)), S).$

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\{\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{2}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-103-0"></span>**Lemma 55.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{3}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ 

*Proof.* The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $u \in [0, |\mathcal{U}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*},j^{*},u}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares  $\sigma_z$  for  $z \in \mathcal{U}|_u$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*,|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the 

{104}------------------------------------------------

lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $u \in [|\mathcal{U}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_{c} \{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the u-th party in  $\mathcal{U}$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,  $h, z, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$  and  $0 < q \leq w$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- $k = i^* \text{ and } t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If  $z < z^*$ : In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w$  neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda} j^*))$  are never called, as both machines output  $(\text{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q))$ , Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q))$ . Notice that  $2^{\lambda} j^*$  and  $W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q$  never intersect, since by assumption  $W_n = \text{poly}(\lambda)$ .
  - If  $z=z^*$ : In this case, neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  are never called, as both machines output:
    - \*  $(x_1, v_1)$  for  $q = w^*$ ,
    - \* (Eval $(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (W^*_{z-1, i^*} + q))$ , Eval $(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (W^*_{z-1, i^*} + q))$ ) for  $0 < q < w^*$ ,
    - \* (Eval $(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda}+q)), S$ ) for  $q > w^*$ , where Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  and Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  are already set within  $x_2$  and  $v_2$ ;
  - If  $z > z^*$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z^{\lambda}}+q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ , whose values are already set within  $x_2$  and  $v_2$ ;
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda}+q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_3^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-104-0"></span>**Lemma 56.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_4^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_5^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the pseudorandomness at punctured points of PPRF (Definition 2) as follows:

– The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$ , the integer n and the unqualified subset  $\mathcal{U} \notin \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{D}}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary  $\mathsf{D}$ .

{105}------------------------------------------------

- The reduction sends to the PPRF security game the point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$  and receives  $K^* = \operatorname{Punc}(K, \{i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)\})$  and either a uniform value  $\bar{u} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  or the value  $\bar{u} = \operatorname{Eval}(K, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$ , where K is the PPRF key generated by the PPRF challenger.
- The reduction proceeds computing:
  - $x_1 = \text{Eval}(\bar{K}_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^* \lambda} + w^*)),$
  - $K_{p,*} = \operatorname{Punc}(K_p, \{i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*)\}),$

•  $x_2 = \text{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j^*)).$ and then the shares for parties  $i \in [n]$ :

• When computing  $\sigma_{i^*}$ : the dealer computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique polynomial of degree  $t_{i^*} - 1$  obtained by interpolating the values:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j), & \text{if } j < j^* \\ \bar{u} & \text{if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K^*, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) & \text{if } j > j^* \end{cases}$$

at the points

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j < j^* \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \geq j^* \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_{i^*,0} = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j^* = 0\\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0) \text{ otherwise} \end{cases}$$

and

$$K_{i^*} = \begin{cases} \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0 \\ m \neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_{i^*,0}-x_m}{x_j-x_m} & \text{if } j^* = 0\\ \text{Eval}(K^*, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0) & \text{otherwise} \end{cases}$$

and sets  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu_b$ . Then, if  $j^* > 0$ , the challenger computes:

$$\mathrm{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{\mathrm{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda}+w^*)) - x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

and if  $i^* = z^*$  sets:

$$\begin{split} M_{i^*} &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, x_1, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*, w^*}^{t_{i^*}}, \\ & x_2, \bar{u}, j^*, w^*, w^*-1], \end{split}$$

otherwise, if  $i^* \neq z^*$ , it sets:

$$\begin{split} M_{i^*} &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, \\ & x_2, \bar{u}, j^*, 0, 0]. \end{split}$$

Finally,  $\sigma_{i^*} = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_{i^*}, \widetilde{M}_{i^*}, x_{i^*,0}).$ 

{106}------------------------------------------------

• When computing  $(\sigma_i)_{i < i^*}$ : the challenger sets  $\operatorname{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Then, if  $i = z^*$ , the dealer sets:

$$\begin{split} M_i &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, x_1, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}, x_2, \\ & \bar{u}, j^*, w^*, w^* - 1], \end{split}$$

otherwise if  $i < z^*$  it sets:

$$\begin{split} M_i &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, \\ & 0, \bot, W_{i,i^*}^*, 0, \mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(i)], \end{split}$$

otherwise if  $i > z^*$  it sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, x_2, \bar{u}, j^*, 0, 0],$$

and finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$  with  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i||t_i||h_i||0)$ .

• When computing  $(\sigma_i)_{i>i^*}$ : the dealer computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i-1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\mathsf{Eval}(K^*,i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  at the points  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p,i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  for all  $j \in [0,t_i)$  and sets  $\mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu_b$ . Then, the dealer sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K^*, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, x_2, \bar{u}, j^*, 0, 0],$$

and finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , with  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0)$ .

- The reduction forwards  $\{\sigma_u\}_{u\in\mathcal{U}}$  to D.
- Finally, the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{4}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{5}^{i^{*},j^{*}}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-106-1"></span>**Lemma 57.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_5^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*)$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_5^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 56 where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{p,*}$  and  $x_2$  (and hence  $x_{j^*}$ ) respectively (instead of  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ), while the point  $v_2$  (and hence  $y_{j^*}$  is randomly sampled). We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-106-0"></span>**Lemma 58.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_6^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by Lemma 1. We can show how to turn any distinguisher D between the two hybrids into an adversary attacking the security of Lemma 1 as follows:

– The reduction receives the messages  $\mu_0, \mu_1 \in \mathcal{M}$ , the integer n and the unqualified subset  $\mathcal{U} \notin \hat{\mathcal{A}}_n^{\mathsf{dw}-\mathsf{ethr}}$  from the  $\mathbf{G}_{\mathsf{SS},\mathsf{D}}^{\mathsf{priv}}$  adversary  $\mathsf{D}$ .

{107}------------------------------------------------

- The reduction sends to the security game of Lemma 1:
  - $\bullet$  n=n;
  - $t = t_{i^*}$ ;

• 
$$\mathcal{I} = \{x_j \mid x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$
with  $|\mathcal{I}| = t_{i^*} - 1$ ;

- $\begin{aligned} &\text{with } |\mathcal{L}| = t_{i^*} 1; \\ &\bullet i_{t-1} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*)); \\ &\bullet i^* = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0) \text{ if } j^* = 0 \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^*\lambda} + w^*)) \text{ otherwise} \end{cases} \\ &\bullet \mathcal{Y} = \{ y_j \mid y_j = \begin{cases} \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases} \end{aligned}$ with  $|\mathcal{Y}| = t_{i^*}$
- The Lemma 1 challenger randomly samples  $y_{t-1}$  and computes  $r_b$  either as a random value or as  $f(i^*) = \sum_{j=0}^{t-1} y_j \ell_j(i^*)$ , where  $\ell_j(x) = \prod_{\substack{0 \le m \le t-1 \\ m \ne j}} \frac{x-x_m}{x_j-x_m}$ .

Then, it forwards  $r_b$  to the reduction.

- The reduction proceeds computing:
  - $K_{p,*} = \operatorname{Punc}(K_p, \{i^* | |t_{i^*}| | h_{i^*}| |(2^{\lambda} j^*)\}),$
  - $$\begin{split} \bullet \ \ K_{f,*}^{r, r} &= \operatorname{Punc}(K_f, \{i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} j^*) \}), \\ \bullet \ \ x_1 &= \operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z^* \lambda} + w^*)) \end{split}$$

and then the shares for parties  $i \in [n]$ :

• When computing  $\sigma_{i^*}$ : the dealer computes  $f_{i^*}(x)$  as the unique polynomial of degree  $t_{i^*} - 1$  obtained by interpolating the values:

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ r_b \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

at the points

$$x_{j} = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p}', i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||h_{i^{*}}||j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^{*}) \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p}, i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||h_{i^{*}}||0) \text{ if } j = j^{*} = 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p}, i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||h_{i^{*}}||(2^{z^{*}\lambda} + w^{*})) \text{ if } j = j^{*} \neq 0 \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_{p}, i^{*}||t_{i^{*}}||h_{i^{*}}||(2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^{*} + 1, t_{i^{*}}) \end{cases}$$

Then the challenger sets:

$$K_{i^*} = \begin{cases} r_b \text{ if } j^* = 0\\ \text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0) \text{ otherwise} \end{cases}$$

and, if  $j^* > 0$ ,  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = r_b$ . Then, the challenger sets

$$v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m},$$

{108}------------------------------------------------

where we recall  $x_2 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  from previous hybrid.

Then, the challenger sets  $\mathsf{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu_b$ . Finally, if  $i^* = z^*$ , the challenger sets:

$$\begin{split} M_{i^*} &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, x_1, \mathsf{sh}_{z^*, w^*}^{t_{i^*}}, \\ & x_2, v_2, j^*, w^*, w^*-1], \end{split}$$

otherwise it sets:

$$M_{i^*} = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i^*-1, i^*}^*, i^*, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0].$$

Finally, 
$$\sigma_{i^*} = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_{i^*}, \widetilde{M}_{i^*}, x_{i^*,0})$$
, where  $x_{i^*,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0)$  if  $j^* = 0$ , while  $x_{i^*,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0)$  if  $j^* > 0$ .

• When computing  $(\sigma_i)_{i < i^*}$ : the challenger sets  $\mathsf{ct}_i \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Then, if  $i = z^*$ , the dealer sets:

$$\begin{split} M_i &= M_p^{\text{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \text{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, x_1, r_b, x_2, v_2, j^*, \\ & w^*, w^* - 1], \end{split}$$

otherwise if  $i > z^*$  it sets:

$$M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0],$$

otherwise if  $i < z^*$ , it sets:

$$\begin{split} M_i &= M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, 0, \bot, W_{i,i^*}^*, \\ & 0, \mathsf{weight}_{i^*}(i)], \end{split}$$

and finally  $\sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0})$ , where  $x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0)$ .

- When computing  $(\sigma_i)_{i>i^*}$ : the dealer computes  $K_i = f_i(0)$  where  $f_i(x)$  is the unique polynomial of degree  $t_i-1$  obtained by interpolating the evaluations  $\operatorname{Eval}(K_f,i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  at the points  $\operatorname{Eval}(K_p,i||t_i||h_i||(2^{\lambda}-j))$  for all  $j \in [0,t_i)$  and sets:
  - $\begin{tabular}{l} * & \mathsf{ct}_i = K_i \cdot \mu_b, \\ * & M_i = M_p^{\mathsf{dw-share}}[K_{f,*}, K_{p,*}, K_p', \mathsf{hk}, W_{i-1,i^*}^*, i, i^*, t_{i^*}, 0, 0, x_2, v_2, j^*, 0, 0] \\ \text{and finally } & \sigma_i = (\mathsf{hk}, \mathsf{ct}_i, \widetilde{M}_i, x_{i,0}), \text{ where } x_{i,0} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i||t_i||h_i||0). \\ \end{tabular}$
- The reduction forwards  $\{\sigma_u\}_{u\in\mathcal{U}}$  to D.
- Finally the reduction outputs whatever D outputs.

It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{6}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b) \equiv \mathbf{H}_{7}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$ .

<span id="page-108-1"></span>**Lemma 59.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_7^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

<span id="page-108-0"></span>*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf, since, as shown in Lemma 55,  $\operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  and  $\operatorname{Eval}(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{\lambda}-j^*))$  are never called. We omit the proof here for brevity.

{109}------------------------------------------------

**Lemma 60.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

Proof. The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $u \in [0, |\mathcal{U}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares  $\sigma_z$  for  $z \in \mathcal{U}|_u$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{8}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $u \in [|\mathcal{U}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the u-th party in  $\mathcal{U}$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,h,  $z, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$ , and  $0 < q \leq w$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- If  $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If  $z < z^*$ : In this case, for every  $0 < q \le w$  neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  and Eval $(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  are never called, as both machines output  $(\text{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q)), \text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q)))$ , and for every  $q \in [w]$  we have that  $W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q \le W_{z,i^*}^* \le W_{z^*-1,i^*}^*$  (since  $z < z^*$ ), and  $W_{z^*-1,i^*}^* < j^*$  by definition, hence  $W_{z-1,i^*}^* + q < j^*$  for every  $q \in [w]$ .
  - If  $z = z^*$ : In this case, neither in  $M_0$  or in  $M_1$  Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  and Eval $(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  are never called, as both machines output:
    - \*  $(x_1, v_1)$  for  $q = w^*$ ;
    - \* (Eval $(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || (W_{z-1, i^*}^* + q))$ , Eval $(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (W_{z-1, i^*}^* + q))$ ) for  $0 < q < w^*$ ;
    - \* (Eval $(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda} + q)), S$ ) for  $w^* < q \le w$ , without ever calling Eval $(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  or Eval $(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  because  $l^*$  is equal to  $j^*$  (hence we exit the while-loop);
  - If  $z > z^*$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\text{Eval}(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z^{\lambda}} + q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  or  $\text{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  because  $l^*$  is equal to  $j^*$ .
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, k||t||h||(2^{z\lambda}+q)), S)$ , without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  or  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$ .

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_8^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-109-0"></span>**Lemma 61.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_9^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0$ , if  $j^*=0$ , and  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z^*-1,i^*}+w^*)$  otherwise. The reduction

{110}------------------------------------------------

for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{9}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 56, where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{p,*}$  and  $x_{i^*,0}$  (if  $j^*=0$ ) and as  $K_{p,*}$  and  $x_1$  (if  $j^*>0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $x_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-110-3"></span>**Lemma 62.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{10}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{11}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{10}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 56, where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K'_{p,*}$  and  $x_{i^*,0}$  (if  $j^*=0$ ) and as  $K'_{p,*}$  and  $x_1$  (if  $j^*>0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $x_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-110-2"></span>**Lemma 63.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{11}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{12}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness of PPRF at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*$ . The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{11}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{12}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is similar to the one used in Lemma 56 where  $K^*$  and  $\bar{u}$  are used as  $K_{f,*}$  and  $K_{i^*}$  (if  $j^*=0$ ) and as  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_1$  (if  $j^*>0$ ) (rather than  $K_{f,*}$  and  $v_2$ ). Moreover  $x_2$  is sampled randomly and  $v_2$  is computed as Lagrange interpolation. We omit it for brevity.

<span id="page-110-1"></span>**Lemma 64.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{12}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*, j^*}_{13}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 60 with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

<span id="page-110-0"></span>**Lemma 65.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [0, W^*_{i^*, i^*}]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , it holds that  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*, j^*}(\lambda, b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

Proof. The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $u \in [0, |\mathcal{U}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares  $\sigma_z$  for  $z \in \mathcal{U}|_u$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $u \in [|\mathcal{U}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the u-th party in  $\mathcal{U}$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,,  $h, z, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$ , and  $0 < q \leq w$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

{111}------------------------------------------------

- $-k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If  $z < z^*$ , for any  $0 < q \le w$ , both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  outputs (Eval $(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} ||$
  - $(W_{z-1,i^*}^*+q))$ ,  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^*+q)));$  If  $z=z^*$ : if  $q=w^*$ ,  $M_1$  outputs  $(x_1,v_1)$  while  $M_0$  outputs  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p',i^*||$  $t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^*+q))$ , Eval $(K_f,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(W_{z-1,i^*}^*+q))$ , which are exactly the same values of  $x_1$  and  $v_1$ ; otherwise, if  $q < w^*$ , both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$ outputs  $(\text{Eval}(K'_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (W^*_{z-1, i^*} + q)), \text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (W^*_{z-1, i^*} + q)))$ q); for  $w^* < q \le w$  the outputs are the same described in the next case;
  - If  $z > z^*$ :  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  differs on how they compute the  $j^*$ -th evaluation of the polynomial. In particular, in  $M_1$  we use  $x_2$  and  $v_2$ , while in  $M_0$ , since we incremented  $l^*$ , we compute the  $j^*$ -th evaluation within the while loop  $(j < l^*)$ . Notice that

$$v_2 = \sum_{j=0}^{t_{i^*}-1} y_j \cdot \prod_{\substack{m=0\\m\neq j}}^{t_{i^*}-1} \frac{x_2 - x_m}{x_j - x_m}$$

with

$$y_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ \mathsf{sh}^{t_{i^*}}_{z^*, w^*} \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

and

$$x_j = \begin{cases} \mathsf{Eval}(K_p', i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j) \text{ if } j \in [0, j^*) \\ x_1 \text{ if } j = j^* \\ \mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{\lambda} - j)) \text{ if } j \in [j^* + 1, t_{i^*}) \end{cases}$$

where:

\*  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K'_n, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j^*),$ 

$$* \operatorname{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || j^*)$$

\*  $\operatorname{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}} = \operatorname{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*).$  Hence, in  $M_1$  the  $j^*$ -th evaluation is basically  $v_2$ , computed as Lagrange interpolation of a polynomial where  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$  is one of the points, while in  $M_0$ , the j\*-th evaluation is directly  $\mathsf{sh}_{z^*,w^*}^{t_{i^*}}$ . It follows that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$ will output (Eval $(K_p, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z\lambda}+q)), S)$  (with exactly the same S).

 $-k \neq i^*$  and  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K_p, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || (2^{z\lambda} +$ (q), S).

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{13}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

<span id="page-111-0"></span>**Lemma 66.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$  and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,W_{i^*,i^*}^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c$  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

{112}------------------------------------------------

Proof. The proof uses the hybrid argument. In particular, for every  $u \in [0, |\mathcal{U}|]$ , let  $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  be the experiment where we change how the challenger computes the shares  $\sigma_z$  for  $z \in \mathcal{U}|_u$ . Clearly,  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,W_{i^*,i^*}^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ , and thus in order to prove the lemma, it suffices to show that, for all  $u \in [|\mathcal{U}|]$ , we have  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ . The latter statement follows by security of Obf. Indeed, the only difference between  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  and  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$  relies in the computation of the share  $\sigma_z$  with z being the u-th party in  $\mathcal{U}$ .

Let us argue that  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  are functionally equivalent.

Assuming that there is an input  $(k, t, h, \pi, w, q)$  for which  $M_0$ ,  $M_1$  produce different outputs, then  $k \geq z$ , t > 0, Verify(hk,  $h, z, w, \pi$ )  $\neq 0$ , and  $0 < q \leq w$  must hold. Otherwise they both output  $\perp$ . We distinguish 2 major cases:

- If  $k = i^*$  and  $t = t_{i^*}$ :
  - If  $z \leq i^*$ : In this case, for every  $0 < q \leq w$ , both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will output  $(\mathsf{Eval}(K'_p, k||t||h||(W^*_{z-1,i^*} + q)), \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, k||t||h||(W^*_{z-1,i^*} + q)))$  without ever calling  $\mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0)$ ;
  - If  $z > i^*$ : Both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will abort;
- $-k \neq i^*$  or  $t \neq t_{i^*}$ : In this case both  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  will never call  $\text{Eval}(K_f, i^* || t_{i^*} || h_{i^*} || 0)$ ;

It follows that there does not exist an input that makes  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  have a different output, thus  $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u-1}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*,u}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable. It follows that  $\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)$  and  $\mathbf{H}_{14}^{i^*,W_{i^*,i^*}}(\lambda,b)$  are indistinguishable.

**Lemma 67.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$  and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{15}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by observing that the two hybrids differs only in the share  $\sigma_{i^*}$ : in the former hybrid  $\operatorname{ct}_{i^*} = K_{i^*} \cdot \mu_b$  is a one-time-pad encryption under a uniform key  $K_{i^*}$ , while in the latter  $\operatorname{ct}_{i^*}$  is sampled uniformly at random, which is identically distributed to a one-time-pad encryption.

**Lemma 68.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$  and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{16}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{17}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 66.

**Lemma 69.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W^*_{i^*,i^*},0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*-1}_{30}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{18}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by SSB being index hiding (Definition 5). The reduction for showing  $\{\mathbf{H}_{30}^{i^*,j^*-1}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}\approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{18}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}$  is analogous to the one used in Lemma 53. We omit it for brevity.

{113}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 65, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 71.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W^*_{i^*,i^*},0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{19}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{20}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 64, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 72.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W^*_{i^*,i^*}, 0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{20}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{21}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by pseudorandomness at the punctured point  $i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*$ . The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 63, with  $K_{i^*} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $K_{i^*} = \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0)$  inverted (if  $j^* = 0$ ), and with  $v_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  and  $v_1 = \mathsf{Eval}(K_f, i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||j^*)$  inverted (if  $j^* > 0$ ).

**Lemma 73.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W_{i^*,i^*}^*, 0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{21}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{22}^{i^*,j^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

**Lemma 74.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W^*_{i^*,i^*},0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{22}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{23}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 61 with  $x_{i^*,0} = \text{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||0)$  and  $x_{i^*,0} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  inverted (if  $j^*=0$ ), and with  $x_1 = \text{Eval}(K_p,i^*||t_{i^*}||h_{i^*}||(2^{z^*\lambda}+w^*))$  and  $x_1 \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  inverted (if  $j^*>0$ ).

**Lemma 75.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ ,  $j^* \in [W^*_{i^*,i^*}, 0]$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{23}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}^{i^*,j^*}_{24}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 54, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 82.** For every  $i^* \in \mathcal{U}$ , and for every  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , it holds that  $\{\mathbf{H}_{30}^{i^*,0}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}} \approx_c \{\mathbf{H}_{31}^{i^*}(\lambda,b)\}_{\lambda \in \mathbb{N}}$ .

*Proof.* The lemma follows by security of Obf. The proof is analogous to that in Lemma 52, with  $M_0$  and  $M_1$  inverted.

**Lemma 83.**  $\{\mathbf{H}_{31}^{|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,0)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}} \equiv \{\mathbf{H}_{31}^{|\mathcal{U}|}(\lambda,1)\}_{\lambda\in\mathbb{N}}.$ 

*Proof.* The lemma follows by simply observing that the distributions of the shares  $(\sigma_u)_{u \in \mathcal{U}}$  is now independent of the message.
